\f0\b\fs63\fsmilli31980 \cf2 Using the Command Line\
Interface\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section explains how to use the command line interface (CLI) to administer the Legrand PDU.\
Note that available CLI commands are model dependent.\
CLI commands are case sensitive.\

\f2\fs24 In This Chapter\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 About the Interface ............................................................................... 294\
Logging in to CLI................................................................................... 294\
The ? Command for Showing Available Commands............................ 296\
Querying Available Parameters for a Command.................................. 297\
Showing Information............................................................................. 297\
Clearing Information ............................................................................. 317\
Configuring the Legrand PDU Device and Network............................. 318\
Load Shedding Configuration Commands............................................ 409\

Actuator Control Operations ................................................................. 414\

Logging out of CLI ................................................................................ 419\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 About the Interface\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The Legrand PDU provides a command line interface that enables data center administrators to perform\
some basic management tasks.\
Using this interface, you can do the following:\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Reset the Legrand PDU\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Display the Legrand PDU and network information, such as the device name, firmware version, IP\
address, and so on\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Configure the Legrand PDU and network settings\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Troubleshoot network problems\
You can access the interface over a local connection using a terminal emulation program such as\
HyperTerminal, or via a Telnet or SSH client such as PuTTY.\

\f3\i Note: Telnet access is disabled by default because it communicates openly and is thus insecure. To enable\
Telnet, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Changing Telnet Settings
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 178).\

\f0\i0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Logging in to CLI\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Logging in via HyperTerminal over a local connection is a little different than logging in using SSH or Telnet.\
If a security login agreement has been enabled, you must accept the agreement in order to complete the\
login. Users are authenticated first and the security banner is checked afterwards.
\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 With HyperTerminal\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can use any terminal emulation programs for local access to the command line interface.\
This section illustrates HyperTerminal, which is part of Windows operating systems prior to Windows Vista.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To log in using HyperTerminal:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. 2. Connect your computer to the product via a local (USB or RS-232) connection.\
Launch HyperTerminal on your computer and open a console window. When the window first opens, it is\
blank.\
Make sure the COM port settings use this configuration:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Bits per second = 115200 (115.2Kbps)\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Data bits = 8\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Stop bits = 1\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Parity = None\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Flow control = None\

\f3\i Tip: For a USB connection, you can determine the COM port by choosing Control Panel > System >\
Hardware > Device Manager, and locating the "Dominion PX2 Serial Console" under the Ports group.\

\f1\i0 3. In the communications program, press Enter to send a carriage return to the Legrand PDU. The\
Username prompt appears.\
4. Type a name and press Enter. The name is case sensitive. Then you are prompted to enter a password.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 5. Type a password and press Enter. The password is case sensitive.\
After properly entering the password, the # or > system prompt appears. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and\
Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 296) in the User Guide for more information.\

\f3\i Tip: The "Last Login" information, including the date and time, is also displayed if the same user account\
was used to log in to this product's web interface or CLI.\

\f1\i0 6. You are now logged in to the command line interface and can begin administering this product.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 With SSH or Telnet\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can remotely log in to the command line interface (CLI) using an SSH or Telnet client, such as PuTTY.\

\f3\i Note: PuTTY is a free program you can download from the Internet. Refer to PuTTY's documentation for\
details on configuration.\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To log in using SSH or Telnet:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Ensure SSH or Telnet has been enabled. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Configuring Network Services
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 173) in the\
User Guide.\
2. Launch an SSH or Telnet client and open a console window. A login prompt appears.\
3. Type a name and press Enter. The name is case sensitive.\

\f3\i Note: If using the SSH client, the name must NOT exceed 25 characters. Otherwise, the login fails.\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 296 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Then you are prompted to enter a password.\
4. 5. Type a password and press Enter. The password is case sensitive.\
After properly entering the password, the # or > system prompt appears. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and\
Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 296) in the User Guide for more information.\

\f3\i Tip: The "Last Login" information, including the date and time, is also displayed if the same user account\
was used to log in to this product's web interface or CLI.\

\f1\i0 6. You are now logged in to the command line interface and can begin administering this product.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Depending on the login name you use and the mode you enter, the system prompt in the CLI varies.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 User Mode: When you log in as a normal user, who may not have full permissions to configure the\
Legrand PDU, the 
\f0\b >
\f1\b0  prompt appears.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Administrator Mode: When you log in as an administrator, who has full permissions to configure the\
Legrand PDU, the 
\f0\b #
\f1\b0  prompt appears.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Configuration Mode: You can enter the configuration mode from the administrator or user mode. In this\
mode, the prompt changes to 
\f0\b config:#
\f1\b0  or 
\f0\b config:> 
\f1\b0 and you can change Legrand PDU device and\
network configurations. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Entering Configuration Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 318).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Diagnostic Mode: You can enter the diagnostic mode from the administrator or user mode. In this mode,\
the prompt changes to 
\f0\b diag:#
\f1\b0  or 
\f0\b diag:>
\f1\b0  and you can perform the network troubleshooting commands,\
such as the ping command. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Entering Diagnostic Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 416).\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Closing a Local Connection\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Close the window or terminal emulation program when you finish accessing the Legrand PDU over the local\
connection.\
When accessing or upgrading multiple Legrand PDUs, do not transfer the local connection cable from one\
device to another without closing the local connection window first.\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 The ? Command for Showing Available Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 When you are not familiar with CLI commands, you can press the ? key at anytime for one of the following\
purposes.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Show a list of main CLI commands available in the current mode.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Show a list of available commands or parameters for the command you type. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Querying Available\
Parameters for a Command
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 297).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b In the administrator mode:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  ?\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b In the configuration mode:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  ?\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b In the diagnostic mode:\

\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 297\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f8\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 diag:#
\f1  ?\
Press Enter after pressing the ? command, and a list of main commands for the current mode is displayed.\

\f3\i Tip: To automatically complete a command after typing part of the full command, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Automatically\
Completing a Command
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 418). To re-execute one of the previous commands, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Retrieving\
Previous Commands
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 418).\

\f0\i0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Querying Available Parameters for a Command\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 f you are not sure what commands or parameters are available for a particular type of CLI command or its\
syntax, you can have the CLI show them by adding a space and the help command (?) or list command (ls)\
to the end of that command. A list of available parameters and their descriptions will be displayed.\
The following shows a few query examples.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To query available parameters for the "show" command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show ?\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To query available parameters for the "show user" command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show user ?\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To query available role configuration parameters:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role ?\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To query available parameters for the "role create" command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role create ?\

\f3\i Tip: To automatically complete a command after typing part of the full command, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Automatically\
Completing a Command
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 418). To re-execute one of the previous commands, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Retrieving\
Previous Commands
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 418).\

\f0\i0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Showing Information\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can use the show commands to view current settings or the status of the Legrand PDU device or part of\
it, such as the IP address, networking mode, firmware version, states or readings of internal or external\
sensors, user profiles, and so on.\
Some "show" commands have two formats: one with the parameter "details" and the other without. The\
difference is that the command without the parameter "details" displays a shortened version of information\
while the other displays in-depth information.\
After typing a "show" command, press Enter to execute it.\

\f3\i Note: Depending on your login name, the # prompt may be replaced by the > prompt. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Different CLI\
Modes and Prompts
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 296).\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 298 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Network Configuration\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command shows all network configuration and all network interfaces' information, such as the IP\
address, MAC address, the Ethernet interface's duplex mode, and the wireless interface's status/settings.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show network\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 IP Configuration\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command shows the IP settings shared by all network interfaces, such as DNS and routes. Information\
shown will include both IPv4 and IPv6 configuration.\

\f3\i Tip: To show IPv4-only and IPv6-only configuration data, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 IPv4-Only or IPv6-Only Configuration
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on\
page 299).\

\f8\i0 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ip common\

\f1 To show the IP settings of a specific network interface, use the following command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ip interface <ETH>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Show the IP-related configuration of the ETH1\
interface.\
eth2 Show the IP-related configuration of the ETH2\
interface.\
wireless Show the IP-related configuration of the\
WIRELESS interface.\
bridge Show the IP-related configuration of the BRIDGE\
interface.\
all Show the IP-related configuration of all interfaces.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data. That\
is, 
\f1\i0 show network ip interface
\f3\i .\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 299\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 IPv4-Only or IPv6-Only Configuration\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 To show IPv4-only or IPv6-only configuration, use any of the following commands.\

\f3\i Tip: To show both IPv4 and IPv6 configuration data, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 IP Configuration
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 298).\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To show IPv4 settings shared by all network interfaces, such as DNS and routes:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ipv4 common\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To show IPv6 settings shared by all network interfaces, such as DNS and routes:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ipv6 common\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To show the IPv4 configuration of a specific network interface:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ipv4 interface <ETH>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To show the IPv6 configuration of a specific network interface:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show network ipv6 interface <ETH>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f6\i0\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Show the IPv4 or IPv6 configuration of the ETH1\
interface.\
eth2 Show the IPv4 or IPv6 configuration of the ETH2\
interface.\
wireless Show the IPv4 or IPv6 configuration of the\
WIRELESS interface.\
bridge Show the IPv4 or IPv6 configuration of the\
BRIDGE interface.\
all Show the IPv4 or IPv6 configuration of all\
interfaces.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data. That\
is, 
\f1\i0 show network ipv4 interface
\f3\i .\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 300 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Network Interface Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command shows the specified network interface's information which is NOT related to IP configuration.\
For example, the Ethernet port's LAN interface speed and duplex mode, or the wireless interface's SSID\
parameter and authentication protocol.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show network interface <ETH>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Show the ETH1 interface's non-IP settings.\
eth2 Show the ETH2 interface's non-IP settings.\
wireless Show the WIRELESS interface's non-IP settings.\
bridge Show the BRIDGE interface's non-IP settings.\
all Show the non-IP settings of all interfaces.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data. That\
is, 
\f1\i0 show network interface
\f3\i .\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Network Service Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command shows the network service settings only, including the Telnet setting, TCP ports for HTTP,\
HTTPS, SSH and Modbus/TCP services, and SNMP settings.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show network services <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i http
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i https
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i telnet
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i ssh
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i snmp
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i modbus
\f1\i0  and 
\f3\i zeroconfig
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Displays the settings of all network services,\
including HTTP, HTTPS, Telnet, SSH and SNMP.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data.\

\f1\i0 http Only displays the TCP port for the HTTP service.\
https Only displays the TCP port for the HTTPS service.\
telnet Only displays the settings of the Telnet service.\
ssh Only displays the settings of the SSH service.\
snmp Only displays the SNMP settings.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 301\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 modbus Only displays the settings of the Modbus/TCP\
service.\
zeroconfig Only displays the settings of the zero configuration\
advertising.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 PDU Configuration\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command shows the PDU configuration, such as the device name, firmware version, model type and\
upper limit of active powered dry contact actuators.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show pdu\

\f1 To show detailed information, add the parameter "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show pdu
\f1  
\f8 details\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Outlet Information\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax shows the outlet information.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show outlets <n>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 To show detailed information, add the parameter "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show outlets <n>
\f1  
\f8 details\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Displays the information for all outlets.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data.\

\f1\i0 A specific outlet\
number\
Displays the information for the specified outlet\
only.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , or a number.\

\f3\i Displayed information:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Without the parameter "details," only the outlet name is displayed. For outlet-switching capable models,\
the outlet state is also displayed.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 With the parameter "details," more outlet information is displayed in addition to the outlet name, such as\
the outlet rating.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 302 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Outlet Group Information\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax shows the outlet group information.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show outletgroups <n>\

\f1 To show detailed information, add the parameter "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show outletgroups <n> details\

\f0\b \cf5 Option 
\f1\b0 \cf3 all 
\f0\b \cf5 Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Displays the information for all outlet groups.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data.\

\f1\i0 A specific outlet\
group number\
Displays the information for the specified outlet\
group only.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , or a number.\

\f3\i Displayed information:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Without the parameter "details," only the group's name, the group's index number, member outlets and\
the group's power state (if it is a switched PDU) are displayed.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 With the parameter "details," more inlet information is displayed in addition to the above outlet group\
information, such as each member outlet's power state.\

\f3\i Tip: Legrand PDU allows you to assign the same name to diverse outlet groups. If this really occurs, you still\
can identify different groups through their unique index numbers.\

\f0\i0\b\fs24 \cf5 Inlet Information\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax shows the inlet information.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show inlets <n>\

\f1 To show detailed information, add the parameter "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show inlets <n>
\f1  
\f8 details\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , or a number.\
there are more than 1 inlet on your PDU.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Displays the information for all inlets.\

\f3\i Tip: You can also type the command without\
adding this option "all" to get the same data.\

\f1\i0 A specific inlet\
number\
Displays the information for the specified inlet only.\
An inlet number needs to be specified only when\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 303\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Displayed information:\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Authentication Settings\

\f4\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b General authentication settings:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 This command displays the authentication settings of the Legrand PDU, including both LDAP and Radius\
settings.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show authentication\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b One LDAP server's settings:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 To show the configuration of a specific LDAP server, assign the desired LDAP server with its sequential\
number in the command. To get detailed information, add "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show authentication ldapServer <server_num>\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show authentication ldapServer <server_num> details\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b One Radius server's settings:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 To show the configuration of a specific Radius server, assign the desired Radius server with its sequential\
number in the command. To get detailed information, add "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show authentication radiusServer <server_num>\

\f1 -- OR--\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show authentication radiusServer <server_num> details\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <server_num> is the sequential number of the specified authentication server on the LDAP or Radius\
server list.\

\f3\i Displayed information:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Without specifying any server, Legrand PDU shows the authentication type and a list of both LDAP and\
Radius servers that have been configured.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 When specifying a server, only that server's basic configuration is displayed, such as IP address and\
port number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 With the parameter "details" added, detailed information of the specified server is displayed, such as an\
LDAP server's bind DN and the login name attribute, or a Radius server's timeout and retries values.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Event Log\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The command used to show the event log begins with 
\f8 show eventlog
\f1 . You can add either the 
\f3\i limit
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i class\

\f1\i0 parameters or both to show specific events.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Show the last 30 entries:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show eventlog\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show eventlog limit <n>\

\f1  
\f0\b Show a specific type of events only:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 show eventlog limit <n> class <event_type>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0  or a number.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Displays all entries in the event log.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 314 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 An integer\
number\
10,000.\
Displays the specified number of last entries in the\
event log. The number ranges between 1 to\
<event_type> is one of the following event types.\

\f0\b \cf5 Event type Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all All events.\
device Device-related events, such as system\
starting or firmware upgrade event.\
userAdministration User management events, such as a new\
user profile or a new role.\
userActivity User activities, such as login or logout.\
pdu Displays PDU-related events, such as entry\
or exit of the load shedding mode.\
sensor Internal or external sensor events, such as\
state changes of any sensors.\
serverMonitor Server-monitoring records, such as a server\
being declared reachable or unreachable.\
timerEvent Scheduled action events.\
webcam Events for webcam management, if available.\
cardReader Events for card reader management, if\
available.\
energywise Cisco EnergyWise-related events, such as\
enabling the support of the EnergyWise\
function.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Note: Legrand PDU does not support features regarding Schroff LHX, modem, Raritan asset management,\
and transfer switch so you can ignore these event types in the CLI.\

\f8 #

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 315
\f2\b0 Server Reachability Information for a Specific Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 To show the server reachability information for a certain IT device only, use the following command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show serverReachability
\f1  
\f8 server <n>\

\f1 To show detailed information, add the parameter "details" to the end of the command.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 show serverReachability
\f1  
\f8 server <n> details\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is a number representing the sequence of the IT device in the monitored server list.\
You can find each IT device's sequence number using the CLI command of 
\f8 show\
serverReachability
\f1  as illustrated below.\

\f3\i Displayed information:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Without the parameter "details," only the specified device's IP address, monitoring enabled/disabled\
state and current status are displayed.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 With the parameter "details," more settings for the specified device are displayed, such as number of\
pings and wait time prior to the next ping.\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Clearing Information\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can use the clear commands to remove unnecessary data from the Legrand PDU.\
After typing a "clear" command, press Enter to execute it.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Note: Depending on your login name, the # prompt may be replaced by the > prompt. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Different CLI\
Modes and Prompts
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 296).\

\f0\i0\b\fs24 \cf5 Clearing Event Log\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command removes all data from the event log.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 clear eventlog\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 clear eventlog
\f1  /y\
If you entered the command without "
\f8 /y
\f1 ," a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Type\

\f8 y
\f1  to clear the event log or 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation.\
If you type y, a message "Event log was cleared successfully" is displayed after all data in the event log is\
deleted.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 318 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Clearing WLAN Log\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command removes all data from the diagnostic log for the wireless LAN (WLAN) connection.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 clear wlanlog\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 clear wlanlog /y\

\f1 If you entered the command without "
\f8 /y
\f1 ," a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Type\

\f8 y
\f1  to clear the WLAN log or 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation.\
If you type y, a message "WLAN log was cleared successfully" is displayed to indicate all data in the WLAN\
log has been deleted.\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Configuring the Legrand PDU Device and Network\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 To configure the Legrand PDU device or network settings through the CLI, it is highly recommended to log in\
as the administrator so that you have full permissions.\
To configure any settings, enter the configuration mode. Configuration commands are case sensitive so\
ensure you capitalize them correctly.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Entering Configuration Mode\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Configuration commands function in configuration mode only.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enter configuration mode:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Ensure you have entered administrator mode and the # prompt is displayed.\

\f3\i Note: If you enter configuration mode from user mode, you may have limited permissions to make\
configuration changes. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 296).\

\f1\i0 2. 3. Type 
\f8 config
\f1  and press Enter.\
The config:# prompt appears, indicating that you have entered configuration mode.\
4. Now you can type any configuration command and press Enter to change the settings.\

\f9\b \cf5 Important: To apply new configuration settings, you must issue the "apply" command before closing the\
terminal emulation program. Closing the program does not save any configuration changes. See 
\f10\i\b0 Quitting\
Configuration Mode
\f9\i0\b  (on page 318).\

\f0\fs24 Quitting Configuration Mode\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Both of "apply" and "cancel" commands let you quit the configuration mode. The difference is that "apply"\
saves all changes you made in the configuration mode while "cancel" aborts all changes.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To quit the configuration mode, use either command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 apply\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 cancel\

\f1 The # or > prompt appears after pressing Enter, indicating that you have entered the administrator or user\
mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 296).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 319\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 PDU Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A PDU configuration command begins with 
\f3\i pdu
\f1\i0 . You can use the PDU configuration commands to change\
the settings that apply to the whole Legrand PDU device.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing the PDU Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command changes the device name of Legrand PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu name "<name>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Outlet Power-On Sequence\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command sets the outlet power-on sequence when the PDU powers up.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletSequence <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i default
\f1\i0 , or a comma-separated list of outlet numbers.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 default All outlets are switched ON in the ASCENDING\
order (from outlet 1 to the final outlet) when the\
Legrand PDU powers up.\
A comma-\
separated list of\
outlet numbers\
All outlets are switched ON in the order you\
specify using the comma-separated list.\
The list must include all outlets on the PDU.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Outlet Power-On Sequence Delay\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command sets the delays (in seconds) for outlets when turning on all outlets in sequence.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 320 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletSequenceDelay <outlet1>:<delay1>;<outlet2>:<delay2>;\
<outlet3>:<delay3>;...\

\f1 Separate outlet numbers and their delay settings with a colon. Outlets followed by delays are separated with\
a semicolon.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <outlet1>, <outlet2>, <outlet3> and the like are individual outlet numbers or a range of outlets using a\
dash. For example, 
\f3\i 3-8
\f1\i0  represents outlets 3 to 8.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <delay1>, <delay2>, <delay3> and the like are the delay time in seconds.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the PDU-Defined Default Outlet State\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines the initial power condition of all outlets after powering up the PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletStateOnDeviceStartup <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i off
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i on
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i lastKnownState
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 off Switches OFF all outlets when the Legrand PDU\
powers up.\
on Switches ON all outlets when the Legrand PDU\
powers up.\
lastKnownState Restores all outlets to the previous status before\
powering down the Legrand PDU when the PDU\
powers up again.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the PDU-Defined Cycling Power-Off Period\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command sets the power-off period of the power cycling operation for all outlets.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu cyclingPowerOffPeriod <timing>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timing> is the time of the cycling power-off period in seconds, which is an integer between 0 and 3600,\
or 
\f3\i pduDefined
\f1\i0  for following the PDU-defined timing.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 321\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Setting the Inrush Guard Delay Time\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command sets the inrush guard delay.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu inrushGuardDelay <timing>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timing> is a delay time between 100 and 100000 milliseconds.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Outlet Initialization Delay\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines the outlet initialization delay timing on device startup. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 PDU
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 102) for\
information on outlet initialization delay.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletInitializationDelayOnDeviceStartup <timing>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timing> is a delay time between 1 and 3600 seconds.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Specifying Non-Critical Outlets\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines critical and non-critical outlets. It is associated with the load shedding mode. See\

\f7\i\b \cf5 Load Shedding Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 112).\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu nonCriticalOutlets <outlets1>:false;<outlets2>:true\

\f1 Separate outlet numbers and their settings with a colon. Separate each "false" and "true" setting with a\
semicolon.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <outlets1> is one or multiple outlet numbers to be set as critical outlets. Use commas to separate outlet\
numbers.\
Use a dash for a range of consecutive outlets. For example, 
\f3\i 3-8
\f1\i0  represents outlets 3 to 8.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <outlets2> is one or multiple outlet numbers to be set as NON-critical outlets. Use commas to separate\
outlet numbers.\
Use a dash for a range of consecutive outlets. For example, 
\f3\i 3-8
\f1\i0  represents outlets 3 to 8.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 322 Legrand PDU User Guide

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Specifying the Device Altitude\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command specifies the altitude of your Legrand PDU above sea level (in meters). You must specify the\
altitude of Legrand PDU above sea level if a Raritan's DPX differential air pressure sensor is attached. This\
is because the device's altitude is associated with the altitude correction factor. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Altitude Correction\
Factors
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 516).\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu deviceAltitude <altitude>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <altitude> is an integer between -425 and 3000 meters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Note that the lower limit "-425" is a negative value because some locations are below the seal level.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 323\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Setting the Z Coordinate Format for Environmental Sensors\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables the use of rack units for specifying the height (Z coordinate) of\
environmental sensors.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu externalSensorsZCoordinateFormat <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i rackUnits
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i freeForm
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 rackUnits The height of the Z coordinate is measured in\
standard rack units.\
When this is selected, you can type a numeric\
value in the rack unit to describe the Z coordinate\
of any environmental sensors or actuators.\
freeForm Any alphanumeric string can be used for\
specifying the Z coordinate.\

\f3\i Note: After determining the format for the Z coordinate, you can set a value for it. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Setting the Z\
Coordinate
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 392).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 324 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Setting the Maximum Number of Active Powered Dry Contact Actuators\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the upper limit of "active" powered dry contact actuators on one Legrand PDU\
device. You need either 'Change Peripheral Device Configuration' privilege or 'Administrator Privileges' to\
change its upper limit.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu activePoweredDryContactLimit <number>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <number> is the number representing the maximum number of active powered dry contact actuators. Its\
value ranges between 
\f3\i 0 to 24
\f1\i0 .\

\f3\i Note: An "active" actuator is the one that is turned ON, or, if with a door handle connected, is OPENED.\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Examples\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section illustrates several PDU configuration examples.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 1 - PDU Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns the name "my px12" to the PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu name "my px12"\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 2 - Outlet Sequence\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command causes a 10-outlet PDU to first power on the 8th to 6th outlets and then the rest of\
outlets in the ascending order after the PDU powers up.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletSequence 8-6,1-5,9,10\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Example 3 - Outlet Sequence Delay\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command determines that the outlet 1's delay is 2.5 seconds, outlet 2's delay is 3 seconds,\
and the delay for outlets 3 through 5 is 10 seconds.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu outletSequenceDelay 1:2.5;2:3;3-5:10\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 4 - Non-Critical Outlets\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets outlets 1, 2, 3, 7, and 9 to be critical outlets, and 4, 5, 6, 8, 10, 11 and 12 to be\
non-critical outlets on a 12-outlet Legrand PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 pdu nonCriticalOutlets 1-3,7,9:false;4-6,8,10-12:true\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Network Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A network configuration command begins with 
\f3\i network
\f1\i0 . A number of network settings can be changed\
through the CLI, such as the IP address, transmission speed, duplex mode, and so on.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Configuring IPv4 Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An IPv4 configuration command begins with 
\f3\i network ipv4
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 325
\f2\b0 Setting the IPv4 Configuration Mode\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the IP configuration mode.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 interface <ETH> configMethod <mode>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Determine the IPv4 configuration mode of the\
ETH1 interface (wired networking).\
eth2 Determine the IPv4 configuration mode of the\
ETH2 interface (wired networking).\
wireless Determine the IPv4 configuration mode of the\
WIRELESS interface (that is, wireless\
networking).\
bridge Determine the IPv4 configuration mode of the\
BRIDGE interface (that is, bridging mode).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <mode> is one of the modes: 
\f3\i dhcp
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i static
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Mode Description\

\f6\b0\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 dhcp The IPv4 configuration mode is set to DHCP.\
static The IPv4 configuration mode is set to static IP\
address.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the IPv4 Preferred Host Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 After selecting DHCP as the IPv4 configuration mode, you can specify the preferred host name, which is\
optional. The following is the command:\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 interface <ETH> preferredHostName <name>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Determine the IPv4 preferred host name of the\
ETH1 interface (that is, wired networking).\
eth2 Determine the IPv4 preferred host name of the\
ETH2 interface (that is, wired networking).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 326 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 wireless Determine the IPv4 preferred host name of the\
WIRELESS interface (that is, wireless\
networking).\
bridge Determine the IPv4 preferred host name of the\
BRIDGE interface (that is, bridging mode).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a host name which:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Consists of alphanumeric characters and/or hyphens\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Cannot begin or end with a hyphen\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Cannot contain more than 63 characters\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Cannot contain punctuation marks, spaces, and other symbols\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the IPv4 Address\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 After selecting the static IP configuration mode, you can use this command to assign a permanent IP\
address to the Legrand PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 interface <ETH> address <ip address>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the network interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ip address> is the IP address being assigned to your Legrand PDU. Its format is "IP address/prefix".\
For example, 
\f3\i 192.168.84.99/24
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Interface Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 Determine the IPv4 address of the ETH1 interface\
(that is, wired networking).\
eth2 Determine the IPv4 address of the ETH2 interface\
(that is, wired networking).\
wireless Determine the IPv4 address of the WIRELESS\
interface (that is, wireless networking).\
bridge Determine the IPv4 address of the BRIDGE\
interface (that is, the bridging mode).\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Setting the IPv4 Gateway\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 After selecting the static IP configuration mode, you can use this command to specify the gateway.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 gateway <ip address>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ip address> is the IP address of the gateway. The value ranges from 0.0.0.0 to 255.255.255.255.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 327
\f2\b0 Setting IPv4 Static Routes\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If the IPv4 network mode is set to static IP and your local network contains two subnets, you can configure\
static routes to enable or disable communications between the Legrand PDU and devices in the other\
subnet.\
These commands are prefixed with 
\f3\i network ipv4 staticRoutes
\f1\i0 .\
Depending on whether the other network is directly reachable or not, there are two methods for adding a\
static route. For further information, see 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Static Route Examples
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 163).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Method 1: add a static route when the other network is NOT directly reachable:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 staticRoutes add <dest-1> <hop>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Method 2: add a static route when the other network is directly reachable:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 staticRoutes add <dest-1> interface <ETH>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Delete an existing static route:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 staticRoutes delete <route_ID>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an existing static route:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  -- OR --\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 staticRoutes modify <route_ID> <dest-2> <hop>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f8\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 network ipv4 staticRoutes modify <route_ID> <dest-2> interface <ETH>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <dest-1> is a combination of the IP address and subnet mask of the other subnet. The format is 
\f3\i IP\
address/subnet mask
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <hop> is the IP address of the next hop router.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the interfaces: 
\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i WIRELESS
\f1\i0  and 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Type "bridge" only when your\
Legrand PDU is in the bridging mode.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <route_ID> is the ID number of the route setting which you want to delete or modify.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <dest-2> is a modified route setting that will replace the original route setting. Its format is 
\f3\i IP\
address/subnet mask
\f1\i0 . You can modify either the IP address or the subnet mask or both.\

\f3\i ETH1/ETH2
\f1\i0 ,

\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i BRIDGE
\f1\i0 . Note that you must\
choose/configure the bridge interface if your Legrand PDU is set to the bridging mode.\

\f3\i Note: In the bridging mode, only the IP parameters of the BRIDGE interface function. The IP parameters\
of ETH1/ETH2 and WIRELESS interfaces do NOT function.\

ETH1 interface (wired networking).\
eth2 Determine the IPv6 configuration mode of the\
ETH2 interface (wired networking).\
wireless Determine the IPv6 configuration mode of the\
WIRELESS interface (that is, wireless\
networking).\
bridge Determine the IPv6 configuration mode of the\
BRIDGE interface (that is, bridging mode).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623

\f3\i automatic
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i static
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Mode Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 automatic The IPv6 configuration mode is set to automatic.\

address.\

\f2 \cf5 Configuring DNS Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Use the following commands to configure static DNS-related settings.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify the primary DNS server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns firstServer <ip address>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify the secondary DNS server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns secondServer <ip address>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify the third DNS server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns thirdServer <ip address>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify one or multiple optional DNS search suffixes:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns searchSuffixes <suffix1>\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns searchSuffixes <suffix1>,<suffix2>,<suffix3>,...,<suffix6>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine which IP address is used when the DNS server returns both IPv4 and IPv6 addresses:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network dns resolverPreference <resolver>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ip address> is the IP address of the DNS server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <suffix1>, <suffix2>, and the like are the DNS suffixes that automatically apply when searching for any\
device via Legrand PDU. For example, <suffix1> can be 
\f3\i raritan.com
\f1\i0 , and <suffix2> can be 
\f3\i legrand.com
\f1\i0 .\
You can specify up to 6 suffixes by separating them with commas.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <resolver> is one of the options: 
\f3\i preferV4
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i preferV6.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 preferV4 Use the IPv4 addresses returned by the DNS\
server.\
preferV6 Use the IPv6 addresses returned by the DNS\
server.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting LAN Interface Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A LAN interface configuration command begins with 
\f3\i network ethernet
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 332 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Enabling or Disabling the LAN Interface\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables the LAN interface.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ethernet <ETH> enabled <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the options -- 
\f3\i eth1
\f1\i0  
\f3\i or eth2
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option 
\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 
\f0\b \cf5 Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 ETH1 port\
eth2 ETH2 port\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  
\f3\i or false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true The specified network interface is enabled.\
false The specified network interface is disabled.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing the LAN Interface Speed\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the LAN interface speed.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ethernet <ETH> speed <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the options -- 
\f3\i eth1
\f1\i0  
\f3\i or eth2
\f1\i0 .\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 ETH1 port\
eth2 ETH2 port\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i auto
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 10Mbps or
\f1\i0  
\f3\i 100Mbps.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 auto System determines the optimum LAN speed\
through auto-negotiation.\
10Mbps The LAN speed is always 10 Mbps.\
100Mbps The LAN speed is always 100 Mbps.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 333
\f2\b0 Changing the LAN Duplex Mode\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the LAN interface duplex mode.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  network ethernet <ETH> duplexMode <mode>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ETH> is one of the options -- 
\f3\i eth1
\f1\i0  
\f3\i or eth2
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 eth1 ETH1 port\
eth2 ETH2 port\
<mode> is one of the modes: 
\f3\i auto
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i half
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i full
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 auto The Legrand PDU selects the optimum\
transmission mode through auto-negotiation.\
half Half duplex:\
Data is transmitted in one direction (to or from the\
Legrand PDU) at a time.\
full Full duplex:\
Data is transmitted in both directions\
simultaneously.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Setting Wireless Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You must configure wireless parameters, including Service Set Identifier (SSID), authentication method,\
Pre-Shared Key (PSK), and Basic Service Set Identifier (BSSID) after the wireless networking mode is\
enabled.\
A wireless configuration command begins with 
\f3\i network wireless
\f1\i0 .\

\f3\i Note: If current networking mode is not wireless, the SSID, PSK and BSSID values are not applied until the\
networking mode is changed to "wireless." In addition, a message appears, indicating that the active network\
interface is not wireless.\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Setting the SSID\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command specifies the SSID string.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless SSID <ssid>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ssid> is the name of the wireless access point, which consists of:\
- Up to 32 ASCII characters\
- No spaces\
- ASCII codes 0x20 ~ 0x7E\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 334 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Setting the Authentication Method\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command sets the wireless authentication method to either PSK or Extensible Authentication Protocol\
(EAP).\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless authMethod <method>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <method> is one of the authentication methods: 
\f3\i PSK
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i EAP
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Method Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 PSK The wireless authentication method is set to PSK.\
EAP The wireless authentication method is set to EAP.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the PSK\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 this command.\
If the Pre-Shared Key (PSK) authentication method is selected, you must assign a PSK passphrase by using\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless PSK <psk>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <psk> is a string or passphrase that consists of:\
- 8 to 63 characters\
- No spaces\
- ASCII codes 0x20 ~ 0x7E\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 335\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Setting EAP Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 When the wireless authentication method is set to EAP, you must configure EAP authentication parameters,\
including outer authentication, inner authentication, EAP identity, password, and CA certificate.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the outer authentication protocol:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless eapOuterAuthentication <outer_auth>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the inner authentication protocol:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless eapInnerAuthentication <inner_auth>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the EAP identity:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless eapIdentity <identity>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the EAP password:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless eapPassword\

\f1 After performing the above command, the Legrand PDU prompts you to enter the password. Then type the\
password and press Enter.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Provide a CA TLS certificate:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless eapCACertificate\

\f1 After performing the above command, the system prompts you to enter the CA certificate's contents. For\
details, see 
\f7\i\b \cf5 EAP CA Certificate Example
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 336).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Enable or disable verification of the TLS certificate chain:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless enableCertVerification <option1>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Allow expired and not yet valid TLS certificates:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless allowOffTimeRangeCerts <option2>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Allow wireless network connection with incorrect system time:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless allowConnectionWithIncorrectClock <option3>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The value of <outer_auth> is 
\f3\i PEAP
\f1\i0  because Legrand PDU only supports Protected Extensible\
Authentication Protocol (PEAP) as the outer authentication.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The value of <inner_auth> is 
\f3\i MSCHAPv2
\f1\i0  because Legrand PDU only supports Microsoft's Challenge\
Authentication Protocol Version 2 (MSCHAPv2) as the inner authentication.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <identity> is your user name for the EAP authentication.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option1> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the verification of the TLS certificate\
chain.\
false Disables the verification of the TLS certificate\
chain.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 336 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Always make the wireless network connection\
successful even though the TLS certificate chain\
contains any certificate which is outdated or not\
valid yet.\
false The wireless network connection is NOT\
successfully established when the TLS certificate\
chain contains any certificate which is outdated or\
not valid yet.\
<option3> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Make the wireless network connection successful\
when the Legrand PDU system time is earlier\
than the firmware build before synchronizing with\
the NTP server, causing the TLS certificate to\
become invalid.\
false The wireless network connection is NOT\
successfully established when the Legrand PDU\
finds that the TLS certificate is not valid due to\
incorrect system time.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option2> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\fs20\fsmilli10020 Mode Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 bridge The Bridging mode, where each cascaded\

portForwarding The Port Forwarding mode, where every\

numbers assigned.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Configuring the Cascading Mode\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the cascading mode.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network <mode> enabled <option1>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <mode> is one of the following cascading modes.\

\f9\b \cf5 Important: When enabling either cascading mode, you must make sure the other cascading mode is disabled, or\
the preferred cascading mode may not be enabled successfully.\

\f2\b0 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option1> is one of the following options:\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b If Port Forwarding mode is enabled, you must configure two more settings to finish the\
configuration:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 On ALL cascaded devices, you must configure the 'role' setting one by one.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network portForwarding role <option2>\

\f1 On the master device, you must configure the 'downstream interface' setting.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network portForwarding\
masterDownstreamInterface <option3>\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true The selected cascading mode is enabled.\
false The selected cascading mode is disabled.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option2> is one of the following cascading roles:\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Role Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 master The device is a master device.\
slave The device is a slave device.\
<option3> is one of the following options:\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 ETH1/ETH2 ETH1/ETH2 port is the port where the 1st\
slave device is connected.\
Usb USB port is the port where the 1st slave\
device is connected.\

\f1\i0 .\
specified NTP server.\

\f1\b0 \cf3 manual The date and time settings are customized.\
ntp The date and time settings synchronize with a\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting NTP Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A time configuration command for NTP-related parameters begins with 
\f3\i time ntp
\f1\i0 .\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify the primary time server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time ntp firstServer <first_server>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Specify the secondary time server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time ntp secondServer <second_server>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To delete the primary time server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time ntp firstServer ""\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To delete the secondary time server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time ntp secondServer ""\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The <first_server> is the IP address or host name of the primary NTP server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The <second_server> is the IP address or host name of the secondary NTP server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of these options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or
\f3\i  false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Mode Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Customized NTP server settings override the\
DHCP-specified NTP servers.\
false Customized NTP server settings do NOT override\
the DHCP-specified NTP servers.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 346 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Customizing the Date and Time\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If intending to manually configure the date and time, use the following CLI commands to specify them.\

\f3\i Note: You shall set the time configuration method to "manual" prior to customizing the date and time. See\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Determining the Time Setup Method
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 345).\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Assign the date:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time set date <yyyy-mm-dd>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Assign the time:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time set time <hh:mm:ss>\

\f0\b \cf5 Variable Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 <yyyy-mm-dd> Type the date in the format of yyyy-mm-dd.\
For example, type 
\f3\i 2015-11-30
\f1\i0  for November 30,\
2015.\
<hh:mm:ss> Type the time in the format of hh:mm:ss in the\
24-hour format.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f1\i0 For example, type 
\f3\i 13:50:20
\f1\i0  for 1:50:20 pm.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Time Zone\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The CLI has a list of time zones to configure the date and time for the Legrand PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time zone\

\f1 After a list of time zones is displayed, type the index number of the time zone or press Enter to cancel.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To set the time zone:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Type the time zone command as shown below and press Enter.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 time zone\

\f1 2. The system shows a list of time zones. Type the index number of the desired time zone and press Enter.\
3. Type 
\f8 apply 
\f1 for the selected time zone to take effect.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Security Configuration Commands\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 348 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Firewall Control\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can manage firewall control features through the CLI. The firewall control lets you set up rules that\
permit or disallow access to the Legrand PDU from a specific or a range of IP addresses.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv4 firewall configuration command begins with 
\f3\i security ipAccessControl ipv4
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv6 firewall configuration command begins with 
\f3\i security ipAccessControl ipv6
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Modifying Firewall Control Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 There are different commands for modifying firewall control parameters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Enable or disable the IPv4 firewall control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 enabled <option>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the default IPv4 firewall control policy for inbound traffic:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 defaultPolicyIn <policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the default IPv4 firewall control policy for outbound traffic:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 defaultPolicyOut <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Enable or disable the IPv6 firewall control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 enabled <option>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the default IPv6 firewall control policy for inbound traffic:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 defaultPolicyIn <policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the default IPv6 firewall control policy for outbound traffic:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 defaultPolicyOut <policy>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 accept Accepts traffic from all IP addresses.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the IP access control feature.\
false Disables the IP access control feature.\
<policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i accept,
\f1\i0  
\f3\i drop
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i reject
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\fs18 Legrand PDU User Guide 349
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 drop Discards traffic from all IP addresses, without\
sending any failure notification to the source host.\
reject Discards traffic from all IP addresses, and an\
ICMP message is sent to the source host for\
failure notification.\

\f3\i Tip: You can combine both commands to modify all firewall control parameters at a time. See\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Managing Firewall Rules\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can add, delete or modify firewall rules using the CLI commands.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv4 firewall control rule command begins with 
\f3\i security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv6 firewall control rule command begins with 
\f3\i security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 Adding a Firewall Rule\

\f1 \cf3 Depending on where you want to add a new firewall rule in the list, the command for adding a rule varies.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new rule to the bottom of the IPv4 rules list:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule add <direction> <ip_mask> <policy>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new IPv4 rule by inserting it above or below a specific rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule add <direction> <ip_mask> <policy> <insert>\
<rule_number>\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule add <direction> <insert> <rule_number>\
<ip_mask> <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new rule to the bottom of the IPv6 rules list:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule add <direction> <ip_mask> <policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new IPv6 rule by inserting it above or below a specific rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule add <direction> <ip_mask> <policy> <insert>\
<rule_number>\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 350 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule add <direction> <insert> <rule_number>\
<ip_mask> <policy>\

\f0\b \cf5 Direction Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 in Inbound traffic.\
out Outbound traffic.\

\f0\b \cf5 Policy Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 accept Accepts traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es).\
drop Discards traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es), without sending any failure\
notification to the source or destination host.\
reject Discards traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es), and an ICMP message is sent to the\
source or destination host for failure notification.\
<insert> is one of the options: 
\f3\i insertAbove 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i insertBelow
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 insertAbove Inserts the new rule above the specified rule\
number. Then:\

\f3\i new rule's number = the specified rule number\

\f1\i0 insertBelow Inserts the new rule below the specified rule\
number. Then:\

\f3\i new rule's number = the specified rule number + 1\
Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <direction> is one of the options: 
\f3\i in
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i out
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ip_mask> is the combination of the IP address and subnet mask values (or prefix length), which are\
separated with a slash. For example, an IPv4 combination looks like this: 
\f3\i 192.168.94.222/24
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i accept,
\f1\i0  
\f3\i drop
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i reject
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f2 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rule_number> is the number of the existing rule which you want to insert the new rule above or below.\

\f2 \cf5 Modifying a Firewall Rule\

\f1 \cf3 Depending on what to modify in an existing rule, the command varies.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv4 rule's IP address and/or subnet mask:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> ipMask\
<ip_mask>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv4 rule's policy:\

\f6\b0\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 351
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> policy\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify all contents of an existing IPv4 rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> ipMask\
<ip_mask> policy <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv6 rule's IP address and/or prefix length:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> ipMask\
<ip_mask>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv6 rule's policy:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> policy\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify all contents of an IPv6 existing rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <direction> <rule_number> ipMask\
<ip_mask> policy <policy>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <direction> is one of the options: 
\f3\i in
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i out
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Direction 
\f1\b0 \cf3 in 
\f0\b \cf5 Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Inbound traffic.\
out Outbound traffic.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rule_number> is the number of the existing rule that you want to modify.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ip_mask> is the combination of the IP address and subnet mask values (or prefix length), which are\
separated with a slash. For example, an IPv4 combination looks like this: 
\f3\i 192.168.94.222/24
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i accept,
\f1\i0  
\f3\i drop
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i reject
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 accept Accepts traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es).\
drop Discards traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es), without sending any failure\
notification to the source or destination host.\
reject Discards traffic from/to the specified IP\
address(es), and an ICMP message is sent to the\
source or destination host for failure notification.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 352 Legrand PDU User Guide

\f3\i in
\f1\i0  or

\f1\i0 .\

out Outbound traffic.\

restrictedServiceAgreement
