\f2\fs18 \cf5 Enabling or Disabling the Restricted Service Agreement\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command activates or deactivates the Restricted Service Agreement.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security restrictedServiceAgreement enabled <option>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the Restricted Service Agreement\
feature.\
false Disables the Restricted Service Agreement\
feature.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 353
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 After the Restricted Service Agreement feature is enabled, the agreement's content is displayed on the login\
screen.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Do either of the following, or the login fails:\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 In the web interface, select the checkbox labeled "I understand and accept the Restricted Service\
Agreement."\

\f3\i Tip: To select the agreement checkbox using the keyboard, first press Tab to go to the checkbox and\
then Enter.\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 In the CLI, type 
\f8 y
\f1  when the confirmation message "I understand and accept the Restricted Service\
Agreement" is displayed.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Specifying the Agreement Contents\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command allows you to create or modify contents of the Restricted Service Agreement.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security restrictedServiceAgreement bannerContent\

\f1 After performing the above command, do the following:\
1. Type the text comprising up to 10,000 ASCII characters when the CLI prompts you to enter the content.\
2. To end the content:\
a. Press Enter.\
b. Type 
\f8 --END--
\f1  to indicate the end of the content.\
c. Press Enter again.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 354 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If the content is successfully entered, the CLI displays this message "Successfully entered Restricted\
Service Agreement" followed by the total number of entered characters in parentheses.\

\f3\i Note: The new content of Restricted Service Agreement is saved only after typing the 
\f11 apply
\f3  command. See\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Quitting Configuration Mode
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 318).\

\f2\i0 \cf5 Example\

\f1 \cf3 The following example illustrates how to specify the content of the Restricted Service Agreement.\
1. Type the following command and press Enter to start entering the content.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security restrictedServiceAgreement bannerContent\

\f1 2. Type the following content when the CLI prompts you to enter the content.\

\f8 IMPORTANT!! You are accessing a PDU. If you are not the system administrator, do\
NOT power off or power cycle any outlet without the permission of the system\
administrator.\

\f1 3. Press Enter.\
4. Type the following:\

\f8 --END--\

\f1 5. Press Enter again.\
6. Verify that the message "Successfully entered Restricted Service Agreement" is displayed, indicating\
that the content input is successful.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Login Limitation\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The login limitation feature controls login-related limitations, such as password aging, simultaneous logins\
using the same user name, and the idle time permitted before forcing a user to log out.\
A login limitation command begins with 
\f3\i security loginLimits
\f1\i0 .\
You can combine multiple commands to modify various login limitation parameters at a time. See\

\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Single Login Limitation\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables the single login feature, which controls whether multiple logins using the\
same login name simultaneously is permitted.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security loginLimits singleLogin <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i enable
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i disable
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 enable Enables the single login feature.\
disable Disables the single login feature.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 355
\f2\b0 Password Aging\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables the password aging feature, which controls whether the password should\
be changed at a regular interval:\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security loginLimits passwordAging <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i enable 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i disable
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 enable Enables the password aging feature.\
disable Disables the password aging feature.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Password Aging Interval\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines how often the password should be changed.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security loginLimits passwordAgingInterval <value>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <value> is a numeric value in days set for the password aging interval. The interval ranges from 7 to 365\
days.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Idle Timeout\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines how long a user can remain idle before that user is forced to log out of the\
Legrand PDU web interface or CLI.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security loginLimits idleTimeout <value>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <value> is a numeric value in minutes set for the idle timeout. The timeout ranges from 1 to 1440\
minutes (24 hours).\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 User Blocking\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 There are different commands for changing different user blocking parameters. These commands begin with\

\f8 security userBlocking
\f1 .\
You can combine multiple commands to modify the user blocking parameters at a time. See\

\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the maximum number of failed logins before blocking a user:\

\fs18 \cf5 356 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security userBlocking maximumNumberOfFailedLogins <value1>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine how long a user is blocked:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security userBlocking blockTime <value2>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <value1> is an integer between 3 and 10, or 
\f3\i unlimited
\f1\i0 , which sets no limit on the maximum number of\
failed logins and thus disables the user blocking function.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <value2> is a numeric value ranging from 1 to 1440 minutes (one day), or 
\f3\i infinite
\f1\i0 , which blocks the user\
all the time until the user is unblocked manually.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Strong Passwords\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The strong password commands determine whether a strong password is required for login, and what a\
strong password should contain at least.\
A strong password command begins with 
\f8 security strongPasswords
\f1 .\
You can combine multiple strong password commands to modify different parameters at a time. See\

\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Enabling or Disabling Strong Passwords\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables the strong password feature.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security strongPasswords enabled <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the strong password feature.\
false Disables the strong password feature.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Minimum Password Length\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the minimum length of the password.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security strongPasswords minimumLength <value>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <value> is an integer between 8 and 32.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Role-Based Access Control\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 In addition to firewall access control based on IP addresses, you can configure other access control rules\
that are based on both IP addresses and users' roles.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv4 role-based access control command begins with 
\f3\i security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv6 role-based access control command begins with 
\f3\i security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6
\f1\i0 .\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Modifying Role-Based Access Control Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 There are different commands for modifying role-based access control parameters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Enable or disable the IPv4 role-based access control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 enabled <option>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the IPv4 role-based access control policy:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 defaultPolicy <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Enable or disable the IPv6 role-based access control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 enabled <option>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the IPv6 role-based access control policy:\

\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 359
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 defaultPolicy <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the role-based access control feature.\
false Disables the role-based access control feature.\
<policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i allow 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i deny
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Policy Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 allow Accepts traffic from all IP addresses regardless of\
the user's role.\
deny Drops traffic from all IP addresses regardless of\
the user's role.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 Tip: You can combine both commands to modify all role-based access control parameters at a time. See\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Managing Role-Based Access Control Rules\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can add, delete or modify role-based access control rules.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv4 role-based access control command for managing rules begins with 
\f3\i security\
roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An IPv6 role-based access control command for managing rules begins with 
\f3\i security\
roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule
\f1\i0 .\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Adding a Role-Based Access Control Rule\

\f1 \cf3 Depending on where you want to add a new rule in the list, the command syntax for adding a rule varies.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new rule to the bottom of the IPv4 rules list:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule add <start_ip> <end_ip> <role>\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new IPv4 rule by inserting it above or below a specific rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule add <start_ip> <end_ip> <role>\
<policy> <insert> <rule_number>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new rule to the bottom of the IPv6 rules list:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule add <start_ip> <end_ip> <role>\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new IPv6 rule by inserting it above or below a specific rule:\

\fs18 \cf5 360 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule add <start_ip> <end_ip> <role>\
<policy> <insert> <rule_number>\

\f0\b \cf5 Policy Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 allow Accepts traffic from the specified IP address\
range when the user is a member of the specified\
role\
deny Drops traffic from the specified IP address range\
when the user is a member of the specified role\
<insert> is one of the options: 
\f3\i insertAbove 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i insertBelow
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 insertAbove Inserts the new rule above the specified rule\
number. Then:\

\f3\i new rule's number = the specified rule number\

\f1\i0 insertBelow Inserts the new rule below the specified rule\
number. Then:\

\f3\i new rule's number = the specified rule number + 1\
Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <start_ip> is the starting IP address.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <end_ip> is the ending IP address.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <role> is the role for which you want to create an access control rule.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i allow
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i deny
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f2 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rule_number> is the number of the existing rule which you want to insert the new rule above or below.\

\f2 \cf5 Modifying a Role-Based Access Control Rule\

\f1 \cf3 Depending on what to modify in an existing rule, the command syntax varies.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv4 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify a rule's IPv4 address range:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <rule_number>\
startIpAddress <start_ip> endIpAddress <end_ip>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv4 rule's role:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <rule_number> role <role>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv4 rule's policy:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <rule_number> policy\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify all contents of an existing IPv4 rule:\

\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 361
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule modify <rule_number>\
startIpAddress <start_ip> endIpAddress <end_ip> role <role> policy <policy>\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f3\i \cf3 IPv6 commands\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify a rule's IPv6 address range:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <rule_number>\
startIpAddress <start_ip> endIpAddress <end_ip>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv6 rule's role:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <rule_number> role <role>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an IPv6 rule's policy:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <rule_number> policy\
<policy>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify all contents of an existing IPv6 rule:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv6 rule modify <rule_number>\
startIpAddress <start_ip> endIpAddress <end_ip> role <role> policy <policy>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rule_number> is the number of the existing rule that you want to modify.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <start_ip> is the starting IP address.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <end_ip> is the ending IP address.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <role> is one of the existing roles.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <policy> is one of the options: 
\f3\i allow
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i deny
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Policy Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 allow Accepts traffic from the specified IP address\
range when the user is a member of the specified\
role\
deny Drops traffic from the specified IP address range\
when the user is a member of the specified role\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Enabling or Disabling Front Panel Outlet Switching\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
The following CLI commands control whether you can turn on or off an outlet by operating the front panel\
display.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enable the front panel outlet control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security frontPanelPermissions add switchOutlet\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To disable the front panel outlet control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security frontPanelPermissions remove switchOutlet\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Enabling or Disabling Front Panel Actuator Control\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following CLI commands control whether you can turn on or off a connected actuator by operating the\
front panel LCD display.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enable the front panel actuator control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security frontPanelPermissions add switchActuator\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To disable the front panel actuator control feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security frontPanelPermissions remove switchActuator\

\f3\i Tip: If your PDU supports multiple front panel permissions, you can combine them into one command by\
adding a semicolon (;) between different permissions. For example, the following CLI command enables both\
front panel actuator control and outlet switching functions simultaneously.\

\f11 security frontPanelPermissions add switchActuator;switchOutlet\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Examples\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section illustrates several security configuration examples.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 1 - IPv4 Firewall Control Configuration\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets up two parameters of the IPv4 access control feature.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 363
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 enabled true defaultPolicyIn accept\
defaultPolicyOut accept\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The IPv4 access control feature is enabled.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The default policy for inbound traffic is set to "accept."\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The default policy for outbound traffic is set to "accept."\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 2 - Adding an IPv4 Firewall Rule\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command adds a new IPv4 access control rule and specifies its location in the list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security ipAccessControl ipv4 rule add 192.168.84.123/24 accept\
insertAbove 5\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 A new IPv4 firewall control rule is added to accept all packets sent from the IPv4 address\
192.168.84.123.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The newly-added rule is inserted above the 5th rule. That is, the new rule becomes the 5th rule, and the\
original 5th rule becomes the 6th rule.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Example 3 - User Blocking\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets up two user blocking parameters.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 security userBlocking maximumNumberOfFailedLogins 5 blockTime 30\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The maximum number of failed logins is set to 5.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The user blocking time is set to 30 minutes.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 4 - Adding an IPv4 Ro le-based Access Control Rule\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command creates a newIPv4 list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  role-based access control rule and specifies its location in the\

\f8 security roleBasedAccessControl ipv4 rule add 192.168.78.50 192.168.90.100\
admin deny insertAbove 3\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 A new IPv4 role-based access control rule is added, dropping all packets from any IPv4 address\
between 192.168.78.50 and 192.168.90.100 when the user is a member of the role "admin."\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The newly-added IPv4 rule is inserted above the 3rd rule. That is, the new rule becomes the 3rd rule,\
and the original 3rd rule becomes the 4th rule.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 364 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Outlet Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An outlet configuration command begins with 
\f3\i outlet
\f1\i0 . Such a command allows you to configure an individual\
outlet.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing the Outlet Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command names an outlet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outlet <n> name "<name>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the outlet that you want to configure.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing an Outlet's Default State\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines the initial power condition of an outlet after the Legrand PDU powers up.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outlet <n> stateOnDeviceStartup <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the outlet that you want to configure.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i off
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i on,
\f1\i0  
\f3\i lastKnownState 
\f1\i0 and
\f3\i  pduDefined.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 off Turn off the outlet.\
on Turn on the outlet.\
lastKnownState Restore the outlet to the state prior to last PDU\
power down.\
pduDefined PDU-defined setting.\

\f3\i Note: Setting the outlet's default state to an option other than 
\f1\i0 pduDefined
\f3\i  overrides the PDU-defined default\
state on that outlet. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Setting the PDU-Defined Default Outlet State
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 320).\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 365\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Setting an Outlet's Cycling Power-Off Period\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines the power-off period of the power cycling operation for a specific outlet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outlet <n> cyclingPowerOffPeriod <timing>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the outlet that you want to configure.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timing> is the time of the cycling power-off period in seconds, which is an integer between 0 and 3600,\
or 
\f3\i pduDefined
\f1\i0  for following the PDU-defined timing.\

\f3\i Note: This setting overrides the PDU-defined cycling power-off period on a particular outlet. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Setting the\
PDU-Defined Cycling Power-Off Period
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 320).\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Example - Outlet Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns the name "Win XP" to outlet 8.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outlet 8 name "Win XP"\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Outlet Group Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An outlet group configuration command begins with 
\f3\i outletgroup
\f1\i0 . Such a command allows you to configure or\
operate an outlet group.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Creating an Outlet Group\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command creates a new outlet group.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup add "<name>" <members>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f3\i Tip: Legrand PDU allows you to assign the same name to diverse outlet groups. If this really occurs, you\
still can identify different groups through their unique index numbers.\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <members> is one or multiple member outlets' index numbers separated with commas. If the member\
outlets are consecutive outlets, you can type a hyphen between the initial and the final index number\
instead of using commas.\
For example, to assign outlets 3, 4, 5, 8 and 10 to the outlet group named "servers", you have two\
choices -- either use a hyphen for consecutive outlets 3 to 5, or use commas for all of member outlets:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup add servers 3-5,8,10\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup add servers 3,4,5,8,10\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 366 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Managing an Outlet Group\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can modify an outlet group's name and member outlets, or simply remove any existing outlet group.\
You can modify both the name and members of an outlet group at a time by combining multiple commands.\
See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an outlet group's name:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup modify <ID> name "<name>"\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify an outlet group's member outlets:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup modify <ID> members <members>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Delete an outlet group:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup delete <ID>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ID> is an outlet group's index number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <members> is one or multiple member outlets' index numbers separated with commas. If the member\
outlets are consecutive outlets, you can type a hyphen between the initial and the final index number\
instead of using commas.\
For example, to assign outlets 3, 4, 5, 8 and 10 to the outlet group named "servers", you have two\
choices -- either use a hyphen for consecutive outlets 3 to 5, or use commas for all of member outlets:\
In the following examples, it is assumed that the "servers" outlet group's index number is 2.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup modify 2 members 3-5,8,10\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f8 outletgroup modify 2 members 3,4,5,8,10\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 367\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Powering On/Off/Cycle Outlet Groups\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Power on one outlet group:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 power outletgroup <ID> on\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Power off one outlet group:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 power outletgroup <ID> off\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Power cycle one outlet group:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 power outletgroup <ID> cycle\

\f1 To quicken the operation, you can add the parameter "/y" to the end of the command, which confirms the\
operation.\
For example:\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 power outletgroup <ID> off /y\

\f1 If you entered the command without "/y", a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Then:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 y
\f1  to confirm the operation, OR\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ID> is an outlet group's index number.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Inlet Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An inlet configuration command begins with 
\f3\i inlet
\f1\i0 . You can configure an inlet by using the inlet configuration\
command.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing the Inlet Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax names an inlet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 inlet <n> name "<name>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the inlet that you want to configure. For a single-inlet PDU, <n> is always 1. The\
value is an integer between 1 and 50.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 368 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Enabling or Disabling an Inlet (for Multi-Inlet PDUs)\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Enabling or disabling an inlet takes effect on a multi-inlet PDU only.\
This command enables or disables an inlet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 inlet <n> enabled <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the inlet that you want to configure. For a single-inlet PDU, <n> is always 1. The\
value is an integer between 1 and 50.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f3\i Note: If performing this command causes all inlets to be disabled, a warning message appears, prompting\
you to confirm. When this occurs, press y to confirm or n to cancel the operation.\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true The specified inlet is enabled.\
false The specified inlet is disabled.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - Inlet Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns the name "AC source" to the inlet 1. If your Legrand PDU contains multiple\
inlets, this command names the 1st inlet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 inlet 1 name "AC source"\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Overcurrent Protector Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An overcurrent protector configuration command begins with 
\f3\i ocp.
\f1\i0  The command configures an individual\
circuit breaker or fuse which protects outlets.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Changing the Overcurrent Protector Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command names a circuit breaker or a fuse which protects outlets on your Legrand PDU.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 ocp <n> name "<name>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the number of the overcurrent protector that you want to configure. The value is an integer\
between 1 and 50.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - OCP Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The command assigns the name "Email servers CB" to the overcurrent protector labeled 2.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 ocp 2 name "Email servers CB"\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 369
\fs24 User Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Most user configuration commands begin with 
\f3\i user
\f1\i0  except for the password change command.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Creating a User Profile\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command creates a new user profile.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user create <name> <option> <roles>\

\f1 After performing the user creation command, the Legrand PDU prompts you to assign a password to the\
newly-created user. Then:\
1. Type the password and press Enter.\
2. Re-type the same password for confirmation and press Enter.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 32 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable CANNOT\
contain spaces.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i enable
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i disable
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <roles> is a role or a list of comma-separated roles assigned to the specified user profile.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 enable Enables the newly-created user profile.\
disable Disables the newly-created user profile.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Modifying a User Profile\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A user profile contains various parameters that you can modify.\

\f3\i Tip: You can combine all commands to modify the parameters of a specific user profile at a time. See\

\f0\i0\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Changing a User's Password\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command allows you to change an existing user's password if you have the Administrator Privileges.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify <name> password\

\f1 After performing the above command, Legrand PDU prompts you to enter a new password. Then:\
1. Type a new password and press Enter.\
2. Re-type the new password for confirmation and press Enter.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is the name of the user whose settings you want to change.\

\f2 \cf5 Example\

\f1 \cf3 The following procedure illustrates how to change the password of the user "May."\
1. Verify that you have entered the configuration mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Entering Configuration Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 318).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 370 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 2. Type the following command to change the password for the user profile "May."\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify May password\

\f1 3. Type a new password when prompted, and press Enter.\
4. Type the same new password and press Enter.\
5. If the password change is completed successfully, the config:# prompt appears.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Modifying a User's Personal Data\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can change a user's personal data, including the user's full name, telephone number, and email\
address.\
Various commands can be combined to modify the parameters of a specific user profile at a time. See\

\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change a user's full name:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify <name> fullName "<full_name>"\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change a user's telephone number:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify <name> telephoneNumber "<phone_number>"\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change a user's email address:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify <name> eMailAddress <email_address>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is the name of the user whose settings you want to change.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <full_name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <full_name> variable must\
be enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <phone_number> is the phone number that can reach the specified user. The <phone_number> variable\
must be enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <email_address> is the email address of the specified user.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Enabling or Disabling a User Profile\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command enables or disables a user profile. A user can log in to the Legrand PDU only after that user's\
user profile is enabled.\

\f8 config:#

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623

\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the specified user profile.\
false Disables the specified user profile.\

\f2\b0 Changing Measurement Units\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 375
\f2\b0 Specifying the SSH Public Key\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If the SSH key-based authentication is enabled, specify the SSH public key for each user profile using the\
following procedure.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To specify or change the SSH public key for a specific user:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Type the SSH public key command as shown below and press Enter.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify <name> sshPublicKey\

\f1 2. The system prompts you to enter the contents of the SSH public key. Do the following to input the\
contents:\
a. Open your SSH public key with a text editor.\
b. Copy all contents in the text editor.\
c. Paste the contents into the terminal.\
d. Press Enter.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To remove an existing SSH public key:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Type the same command as shown above.\
2. When the system prompts you to input the contents, press Enter without typing or pasting anything.\

\f2 \cf5 Example\

\f1 \cf3 The following procedure illustrates how to change the SSH public key for the user "assistant."\
1. Verify that you have entered the configuration mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Entering Configuration Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 318).\
2. Type the following command and press Enter.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify assistant sshPublicKey\

\f1 3. 4. You are prompted to enter a new SSH public key.\
Type the new key and press Enter.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Changing Your Own Password\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Every user can change their own password via this command if they have the Change Own Password\
privilege. Note that this command does not begin with 
\f3\i user
\f1\i0 .\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 password\

\f1 After performing this command, the Legrand PDU prompts you to enter both current and new passwords\
respectively.\

\f9\b \cf5 Important: After the password is changed successfully, the new password is effective immediately no matter you\
type the command "apply" or not to save the changes.\

\f2\b0\fs18 Example\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This procedure changes your own password:\
1. Verify that you have entered the configuration mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Entering Configuration Mode
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 318).\
2. Type the following command and press Enter.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 password\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 376 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 3. Type the existing password and press Enter when the following prompt appears.\

\f8 Current password:\

\f1 4. Type the new password and press Enter when the following prompt appears.\

\f8 Enter new password:\

\f1 5. Re-type the new password for confirmation and press Enter when the following prompt appears.\

\f8 Re-type new password:\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting Default Measurement Units\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Default measurement units, including temperature, length, and pressure units, apply to the Legrand PDU\
user interfaces across all users except for those whose preferred measurement units are set differently by\
themselves or the administrator. Diverse measurement unit commands can be combined so that you can set\
all default measurement units at a time. To combine all commands, see 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page\
408).\

\f3\i Note: The measurement unit change only applies to the web interface and command line interface.\
Tip: To change the preferred measurement units displayed in the Legrand PDU user interfaces for a specific\
user via CLI, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Changing Measurement Units
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 374).\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the default temperature unit:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user defaultpreferences preferredTemperatureUnit <option1>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option1> is one of the options: 
\f3\i C
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i F
\f1\i0 .\
in Celsius.\
in\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 C This option displays the temperature F This option displays the temperature Fahrenheit.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f4\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the default length unit:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user defaultpreferences preferredLengthUnit <option2>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option2> is one of the options: 
\f3\i meter 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i feet
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 meter This option displays the length or height in\
meters.\
feet This option displays the length or height in feet.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command creates a new user profile and sets two parameters for the new user.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user create May enable admin\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 A new user profile "May" is created.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The new user profile is enabled.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The 
\f0\b admin
\f1\b0  role is assigned to the new user profile.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Example 2 - Modifying a User's Roles\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns two roles to the user "May."\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 user modify May roles admin,tester\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The user May has the union of all privileges of "admin" and "tester."\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 3 - Default Measurement Units\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets all default measurement units at a time.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 378 Legrand PDU User Guide

\f8 user defaultpreferences preferredTemperatureUnit F preferredLengthUnit feet\
preferredPressureUnit psi\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The default temperature unit is set to Fahrenheit.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The default length unit is set to feet.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The default pressure unit is set to psi.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Role Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A role configuration command begins with 
\f3\i role
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Creating a Role\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command creates a new role, with a list of semicolon-separated privileges assigned to the role.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role create <name> <privilege1>;<privilege2>;<privilege3>...\

\f1 If a specific privilege contains any arguments, that privilege should be followed by a colon and the\
argument(s).\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role create <name> <privilege1>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege2>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege3>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
...\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 32 ASCII printable characters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <privilege1>, <privilege2>, <privilege3> and the like are names of the privileges assigned to the role.\
Separate each privilege with a semi-colon. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 All Privileges
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 378).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <argument1>, <argument2> and the like are arguments set for a particular privilege. Separate a privilege\
and its argument(s) with a colon, and separate arguments with a comma if there are more than one\
argument for a privilege.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 All Privileges\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This table lists all privileges. Note that available privileges vary according to the model you purchased. For\
example, a PDU without the outlet switching function does not have the privilege "switchOutlet."\

\f0\b \cf5 Privilege Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 acknowledgeAlarms Acknowledge Alarms\
adminPrivilege Administrator Privileges\
changeAssetStripConfiguration Change Asset Strip\
Configuration\
changeAuthSettings Change Authentication Settings\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 379
\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Privilege Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 changeDataTimeSettings Change Date/Time Settings\
changeExternalSensorsConfiguration Change Peripheral Device\
Configuration\
changeLhxConfiguration Change LHX/SHX\
Configuration\
changeModemConfiguration Change Modem Configuration\
changeNetworkSettings Change Network Settings\
changePassword Change Own Password\
changePduConfiguration Change Pdu, Inlet, Outlet &\
Overcurrent Protector\
Configuration\
changeSecuritySettings Change Security Settings\
changeSnmpSettings Change SNMP Settings\
changeUserSettings Change Local User\
Management\
changeWebcamSettings Change Webcam Configuration\
clearLog Clear Local Event Log\
firmwareUpdate Firmware Update\
performReset Reset (Warm Start)\
switchActuator* Switch Actuator\
switchOutlet** Switch Outlet\
viewEventSetup View Event Settings\
viewEverything Unrestricted View Privileges\
viewLog View Local Event Log\
viewSecuritySettings View Security Settings\
viewSnmpSettings View SNMP Settings\
viewUserSettings View Local User Management\
viewWebcamSettings View Webcam Snapshots and\
Configuration\
* The "switchActuator" privilege requires an argument that is separated with a colon. The argument could be:\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 All actuators, that is,\

\f8 switchActuator:all\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An actuator's ID number. For example:\

\f8 switchActuator:1\
switchActuator:2\
switchActuator:3\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 A list of comma-separated ID numbers of different actuators. For example:\

\f8 switchActuator:1,3,6\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 380 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f3\i\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Note: The ID number of each actuator is shown in the Legrand PDU web interface. It is an integer\
between 1 and 32.\

\f1\i0 ** The "switchOutlet" privilege requires an argument that is separated with a colon. The argument could be:\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 All outlets, that is,\

\f8 switchOutlet:all\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 An outlet number. For example:\

\f8 switchOutlet:1\
switchOutlet:2\
switchOutlet:3\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 A list of comma-separated outlets. For example:\

\f8 switchOutlet:1,3,5,7,8,9\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Modifying a Role\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can modify diverse parameters of an existing role, including its privileges.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify a role's description:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role modify <name> description "<description>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 32 ASCII printable characters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <description> is a description comprising alphanumeric characters. The <description> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add more privileges to a specific role:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role modify <name> addPrivileges\
<privilege1>;<privilege2>;<privilege3>...\

\f1 If a specific privilege contains any arguments, add a colon and the argument(s) after that privilege.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 381\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f8\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role modify <name> addPrivileges\
<privilege1>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege2>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege3>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
...\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 32 ASCII printable characters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <privilege1>, <privilege2>, <privilege3> and the like are names of the privileges assigned to the role.\
Separate each privilege with a semi-colon. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 All Privileges
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 378).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <argument1>, <argument2> and the like are arguments set for a particular privilege. Separate a privilege\
and its argument(s) with a colon, and separate arguments with a comma if there are more than one\
argument for a privilege.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Remove specific privileges from a role:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role modify <name> removePrivileges\
<privilege1>;<privilege2>;<privilege3>...\

\f1 If a specific privilege contains any arguments, add a colon and the argument(s) after that privilege.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 role modify <name> removePrivileges\
<privilege1>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege2>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
<privilege3>:<argument1>,<argument2>...;\
...\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Note: When removing privileges from a role, make sure the specified privileges and arguments (if any)\
exactly match those assigned to the role. Otherwise, the command fails to remove specified privileges that\
are not available.\
Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 32 ASCII printable characters.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <privilege1>, <privilege2>, <privilege3> and the like are names of the privileges assigned to the role.\
Separate each privilege with a semi-colon. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 All Privileges
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 378).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <argument1>, <argument2> and the like are arguments set for a particular privilege. Separate a privilege\
and its argument(s) with a colon, and separate arguments with a comma if there are more than one\
argument for a privilege.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Authentication Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An authentication configuration command begins with 
\f3\i authentication
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Determining the Authentication Method\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can choose to set the authentication type only, or both set the authentication type and determine\
whether to switch to local authentication in case the remote authentication is not available.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the authentication type only:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication type <option1>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the authentication type and enable/disable the option of switching to local\
authentication:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication type <option1> useLocalIfRemoteUnavailable <option2>\

\f3\i Note: You cannot enable or disable the option of switching to local authentication without determining the\
authentication type in the CLI. Therefore, always type "authentication type <option1>" when setting up\
"useLocalIfRemoteUnavailable".\

\f6\i0\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option1> is one of the options: 
\f3\i local
\f1\i0  , 
\f3\i ldap
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i radius
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 of the availability of remote authentication.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 local Enable Local authentication only.\
ldap Enable LDAP authentication.\
radius Enable Radius authentication.\
<option2> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Remote authentication is the first priority. The\
device will switch to local authentication when the\
remote authentication is not available.\
false Always stick to remote authentication regardless\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 383
\f2\b0 LDAP Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 All LDAP-related commands begin with 
\f3\i authentication ldap
\f1\i0 .\
If you enable LDAP authentication, you must add at least one LDAP server. Later you can modify or delete\
any existing LDAP server as needed.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Adding an LDAP Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Adding an LDAP server requires the entry of quite a lot of parameters, such as the server's IP address, TCP\
port number, Base DN and so on.\
You can repeat the following CLI command to add more than one LDAP server.\

\f3\i Tip: If any LDAP server's settings are identical to an existing LDAP server's, you can add it by just copying\
the existing one, instead of using the following command. See 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Copying an Existing Server's Settings
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on\
page 386).\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add a new LDAP server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add <host> <port> <ldap_type> <security>\
<bind_type> <base_DN> <login_name_att> <user_entry_class>\

\f0\b "Optional Parameters"\

\f3\i\b0 Note: 
\f7\b "Optional Parameters"
\f3\b0  refer to one or multiple parameters listed in the section 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Optional Parameters\

\f3\i\b0 \cf3 (on page 384). They are required only when your server settings need to specify these parameters. For\
example, if setting the <bind_type> to "authenticatedBind", then you must add the parameter "bindDN" to this\
command.\

\f1\i0 When the above command is successfully performed, a list of all LDAP servers, including the newly-added\
one, will be displayed, which is similar to the following diagram.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Tip: To verify all settings of a newly-added server, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Authentication Settings
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 311).\
Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the IP address or host name of the LDAP server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <port> is the port number assigned for communication with the LDAP server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <ldap_type> is one of the LDAP server types: 
\f3\i openldap
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i activeDirectory
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Type Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 openldap
\f1  OpenLDAP server\

\f8 activeDirectory
\f1  Microsoft Active Directory\
<security> is one of the security options: 
\f3\i none
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i startTls
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i tls
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Type Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 none
\f1  No security\

\f8 startTls
\f1  StartTLS\

\f8 tls
\f1  TLS\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 384 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Type Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 anonymousBind
\f1  Enable the anonymous Bind.\
Bind DN and password are NOT\
required.\

\f8 authenticatedBind
\f1  Enable the Bind with authentication.\
Bind DN and password are required.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <bind_type> is one of the bind options: 
\f3\i anonymouseBind
\f1\i0 , or 
\f3\i authenticatedBind
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <base_DN> is the base DN for search.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <login_name_att> is the login name attribute.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <user_entry_class> is the User Entry Object Class.\

\f2 \cf5 Optional Parameters\

\f1 \cf3 You can add one or multiple "optional parameters", such as specifying the Bind DN or certificate upload, to\
an LDAP-server-adding command as illustrated below. If adding multiple optional parameters, you must add\
them to the END of the command and separate them with a space.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f3\i Example 1 -- Specify an Active Directory Domain's name:\

\f8\i0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add <host> <port> <ldap_type> <security>\
<bind_type> <base_DN> <login_name_att> <user_entry_class>\

\f0\b adDomain <AD_domain>\

\f8\i0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add <host> <port> <ldap_type> <security>\
<bind_type> <base_DN> <login_name_att> <user_entry_class> 
\f0\b bindDN\
<bind_DN>\

\f8 allowExpiredCertificate\
<allow_exp_cert>\

\f1 Whether to accept expired or not valid yet\
certificate\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 385\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <filter> is the user search subfilter you specify.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <bind_DN> is bind DN.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <AD_domain> is the Active Directory Domain.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <verify_cert> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Option Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 true
\f1  Enable the verification of the LDAP server\
certificate.\

\f8 false
\f1  Disable the verification of the LDAP server\
certificate.\
<allow_exp_cert> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 true
\f1  Certificates that are either expired or not valid yet\
are all accepted.\

\f8 false
\f1  Only valid certificates are accepted.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Illustrations of Adding LDAP Servers\

\f1 \cf3 This section shows several LDAP command examples. Those words highlighted in bold are required for their\
respective examples.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b An OpenLDAP server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add op-ldap.raritan.com 389 
\f0\b openldap
\f8\b0  none\
anonymousBind dc=raritan,dc=com 
\f0\b uid
\f8\b0  
\f0\b inetOrgPerson\

\f4\b0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b A Microsoft Active Directory server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add ac-ldap.raritan.com 389 
\f0\b activeDirectory
\f8\b0  none\
anonymousBind dc=raritan,dc=com 
\f0\b sAMAccountName
\f8\b0  
\f0\b user
\f8\b0  
\f0\b adDomain\
raritan.com\

\f4\b0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b An LDAP server with a TLS certificate uploaded:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 a. Enter the CLI command with the following two TLS-related options set and/or added:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f3\i <security> is set to tls or startTls.\

\f5\i0 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f3\i The "verifyServerCertificate" parameter is added to the command and set to "true."\

\f8\i0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add ldap.raritan.com 389 openldap 
\f0\b startTls 
\f8\b0 ...\
inetOrgPerson 
\f0\b verifyServerCertificate true\

\f1\b0 b. The system now prompts you to enter the certificate's content.\
c. Type or copy the certificate's content in the CLI and press Enter.\

\f3\i Note: The certificate's content is located between the line containing "BEGIN CERTIFICATE" and the line\
containing "END CERTIFICATE".\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b An LDAP server with the bind DN and bind password configured:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 a. Enter the CLI command with the "bindDN" parameter and its data added.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 386 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap add op-ldap.raritan.com 389 openldap none\

\f0\b authenticatedBind
\f8\b0  cn=Manager,dc=raritan,dc=com uid inetOrgPerson\

\f0\b bindDN user@raritan.com\

\f1\b0 b. c. The system prompts you to specify the bind DN password.\
Type the password and press Enter.\
d. Re-type the same password.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Copying an Existing Server's Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If the server that you will add completely shares the same settings with any server that has been configured,\
use the following command.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Add an LDAP server by copying an existing server's settings:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap addClone <server_num> <host>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the IP address or host name of the LDAP server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <server_num> is the sequential number of the specified server shown on the server list of the Legrand\
PDU. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Authentication Settings
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 311).\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Modifying an Existing LDAP Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can modify one or multiple parameters of an existing LDAP server, such as its IP address, TCP port\
number, Base DN and so on. Besides, you can also change the priority or sequence of existing LDAP\
servers in the server list.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Command syntax:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 A command to modify an existing LDAP server's settings looks like the following:\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap modify <server_num> 
\f0\b "parameters"\

\f3\i\b0 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <server_num> is the sequential number of the specified server in the LDAP server list.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 Replace 
\f0\b "parameters"
\f1\b0  with one or multiple commands in the following table, depending on which\
parameter(s) you want to modify.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b A list of "parameters":\

\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 387\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Parameters Description\
host <host> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the IP address or host name.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <host> is the new IP address or host name.\

\f0\b \cf5 port <port> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the TCP port number.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <port> is the new TCP port number.\

\f0\b \cf5 serverType <ldap_type> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the server type.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <ldap_type> is the new type of the LDAP server.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <ldap_type> values include: 
\f8 openldap
\f1  and\

\f8 activeDirectory.\

\f0\b \cf5 securityType <security> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the security type.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <security> is the new security type.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <security> values include: 
\f8 none
\f1 , 
\f8 startTls
\f1 , and 
\f8 ssl\

\f0\b \cf5 bindType <bind_type> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the bind type.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <bind_type> is the new bind type.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <bind_type> values include: 
\f8 anonymousBind
\f1  and\

\f8 authenticatedBind.\

\f0\b \cf5 searchBaseDN <base_DN> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the base DN for search.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <base_DN> is the new base DN for search.\

\f0\b \cf5 loginNameAttribute\
<login_name_att>\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the login name attribute.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <login_name_att> is the new login name attribute.\

\f0\b \cf5 userEntryObjectClass\
<user_entry_class>\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the user entry object class.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <user_entry_class> is the new user entry class.\

\f0\b \cf5 userSearchSubfilter\
<user_search_filter>\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the user search subfilter.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <user_search_filter> is the new user search subfilter.\

\f0\b \cf5 adDomain <AD_domain> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the Active Directory Domain name.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <AD_domain> is the new domain name of the Active\
Directory.\

\f0\b \cf5 verifyServerCertificate\
<verify_cert>\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Enable or disable the certificate verification.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <verify_cert> enables or disables the certificate verification\
feature.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Available values include: 
\f8 true
\f1 , 
\f8 false\

\f0\b \cf5 certificate 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Re-upload a different certificate.\
a. First add the "certificate" parameter to the command, and\
press Enter.\
b. The system prompts you for the input of the certificate.\
c. Type or copy the content of the certificate in the CLI and\
press Enter.\

\f0\b \cf5 allowExpiredCertificate\
<allow_exp_cert>\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Determine whether to accept a certificate which is expired or\
not valid yet.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <allow_exp_cert> determines whether to accept an expired\
or not valid yet certificate\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <allow_exp_cert> values include: 
\f8 true
\f1 , and 
\f8 false\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 388 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Parameters Description\
bindDN <bind_DN> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the bind DN.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <bind_DN> is the new bind DN.\

\f0\b \cf5 bindPassword 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the bind DN password.\
a. First add the "bindPassword" parameter to the command,\
and press Enter.\
b. The system prompts you for the input of the password.\
c. Type the password and press Enter.\

\f0\b \cf5 sortPosition <position> 
\f1\b0 \cf3 Change the priority of the server (that is, resorting).\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <position> is the new sequential number of the server in\
the LDAP server list.\

\f3\i Note: For details of the above variables' values, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Adding an LDAP Server
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 383).\

\f4\i0 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Examples:\

\f2\b0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Change the IP address of the 1st LDAP server\

\f8\b0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap modify 1 host 192.168.3.3\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Change both the IP address and TCP port of the 1st LDAP server\

\f8\b0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap modify 1 host 192.168.3.3 port 633\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Change the IP address, TCP port and the type of the L1st DAP server\

\f8\b0 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap modify 1 host 192.168.3.3 port 633\
serverType activeDirectory\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Removing an Existing LDAP Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command removes an existing LDAP server from the server list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication ldap delete <server_num>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <server_num> is the sequential number of the specified server in the LDAP server list.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Radius Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 All Radius-related commands begin with 
\f3\i authentication radius
\f1\i0 .\
If you enable Radius authentication, you must add at least one Radius server. Later you can modify or delete\
any existing Radius server as needed.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Adding a Radius Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can repeat the following commands to add Radius servers one by one.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Command syntax:\

\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 389\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f8\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius add <host> <rds_type> <auth_port> <acct_port> <timeout>\
<retries>\

\f0\b \cf5 Type Description\

\f8\b0 \cf3 chap
\f1  CHAP\

\f8 pap
\f1  PAP\

\f8 msChapV2
\f1  MSCHAP v2\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the IP address or host name of the Radius server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rds_type> is one of the Radius authentication types: 
\f3\i pap, chap, msChapV2
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <auth_port> is the authentication port number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <acct_port> is the accounting port number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timeout> is the timeout value in seconds. It ranges between 1 to 10 seconds.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <retries> is the number of retries. It ranges between 0 to 5.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enter the shared secret:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. After executing the above Radius command, the system automatically prompts you to enter the shared\
secret.\
2. Type the secret and press Enter.\
3. Re-type the same secret and press Enter.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Example:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius add 192.168.7.99 chap 1812 1813 10 3\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Modifying an Existing Radius Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can modify one or multiple parameters of an existing Radius server, or change the priority or sequence\
of existing servers in the server list.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the IP address or host name:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> host <host>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the Radius authentication type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> authType <rds_type>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the authentication port:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> authPort <auth_port>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the accounting port:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> accountPort <acct_port>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the timeout value:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> timeout <timeout>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the number of retries:\

\fs18 \cf5 390 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> retries <retries>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the shared secret:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> secret\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Change the priority of the specified server:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius modify <server_num> sortPositon <position>\

\f3\i Tip: You can add more than one parameters to the command. For example, "
\f11 authentication radius\
modify <server_num> 
\f7\b host <host>
\f11\b0  authType <rds_type> 
\f7\b authPort <auth_port>
\f11\b0  accountPort\
<acct_port> 
\f3 ...".\
Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <server_num> is the sequential number of the specified server in the Radius server list.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the new IP address or host name of the Radius server.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <rds_type> is one of the Radius authentication types: 
\f3\i pap, chap, msChapV2
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <auth_port> is the new authentication port number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <acct_port> is the new accounting port number.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <timeout> is the new timeout value in seconds. It ranges between 1 to 10 seconds.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <retries> is the new number of retries. It ranges between 0 to 5.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enter the shared secret:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. After executing the above Radius command, the system automatically prompts you to enter the shared\
secret.\
2. 3. Type the secret and press Enter.\
Re-type the same secret and press Enter.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Example:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius add 192.168.7.99 chap 1812 1813 10 3\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Removing an Existing Radius Server\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command removes an existing Radius server from the server list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 authentication radius delete <server_num>\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Environmental Sensor Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An environmental sensor configuration command begins with 
\f3\i externalsensor
\f1\i0 . You can configure the name\
and location parameters of an individual environmental sensor.\

\f3\i Note: To configure an actuator, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Actuator Configuration Commands
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 403).\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 391\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Changing the Sensor Name\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command names an environmental sensor.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor <n> name "<name>"\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the ID number of the environmental sensor that you want to configure. The ID number is available\
in the Legrand PDU web interface or using the command "
\f8 show externalsensors <n>
\f1 " in the CLI. It is\
an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f3\i Note: To name an actuator, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Actuator Configuration Commands
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 403).\

\f2\i0\fs18 \cf5 Specifying the CC Sensor Type\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Raritan's contact closure sensor (DPX-CC2-TR) supports the connection of diverse third-party or Raritan's\
detectors/switches. You must specify the type of connected detector/switch for proper operation. Use this\
command when you need to specify the sensor type.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor <n> sensorSubType <sensor_type>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the ID number of the environmental sensor that you want to configure. The ID number is available\
in the Legrand PDU web interface or using the command "
\f8 show externalsensors <n>
\f1 " in the CLI. It is\
an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <sensor_type> is one of these types: 
\f3\i contact
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i smokeDetection
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i waterDetection
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i vibration
\f1\i0 .\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Type Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 contact The connected detector/switch is for detection of\
door lock or door closed/open status.\
smokeDetection The connected detector/switch is for detection of\
the smoke presence.\
waterDetection The connected detector/switch is for detection of\
the water presence.\
vibration The connected detector/switch is for detection of\
the vibration.\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623

\f8 show externalsensors <n>
\f1 " in the CLI. It is\
an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <coordinate> is a string comprising up to 24 ASCII printable characters, and it must be enclosed in\
quotes.\

\f2 \cf5 Using Default Thresholds\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines whether default thresholds, including the deassertion hysteresis and assertion\
timeout, are applied to a specific environmental sensor.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor <n> useDefaultThresholds <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the ID number of the environmental sensor that you want to configure. The ID number is available\
in the Legrand PDU web interface or using the command "
\f8 show externalsensors <n>
\f1 " in the CLI. It is\
an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Default thresholds are selected as the threshold\
option for the specified sensor.\
false Sensor-specific thresholds are selected as the\
threshold option for the specified sensor.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Alarmed to Normal Delay for DX-PIR\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command determines the value of the Alarmed to Normal Delay setting for a DX-PIR presence detector.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor <n> alarmedToNormalDelay <time>\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the ID number of the environmental sensor that you want to configure. The ID number is available\
in the Legrand PDU web interface or using the command "
\f8 show externalsensors <n>
\f1 " in the CLI. It is\
an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <time> is an integer number in seconds, ranging between 0 and 300.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Examples\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section illustrates several environmental sensor configuration examples.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 1 - Environmental Sensor Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns the name "Cabinet humidity" to the environmental sensor with the ID\
number 4.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor 4 name "Cabinet humidity"\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 2 - Sensor Threshold Selection\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets the environmental sensor #1 to use the default thresholds, including the\
deassertion hysteresis and assertion timeout, as its threshold settings.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 externalsensor 1 useDefaultThresholds true\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 394 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Configuring Environmental Sensors' Default Thresholds\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can set the default values of upper and lower thresholds, deassertion hysteresis and assertion timeout\
on a sensor type basis, including temperature, humidity, air pressure and air flow sensors. The default\
thresholds automatically apply to all environmental sensors that are newly detected or added.\
A default threshold configuration command begins with 
\f3\i defaultThresholds
\f1\i0 .\
You can configure various default threshold settings for the same sensor type at a time by combining\
multiple commands. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 408).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Upper Critical Threshold for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> upperCritical <value>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Upper Warning Threshold for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> upperWarning <value>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Lower Critical Threshold for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> lowerCritical <value>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Lower Warning Threshold for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> lowerWarning <value>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Deassertion Hysteresis for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> hysteresis <hy_value>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Set the Default Assertion Timeout for a specific sensor type:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds <sensor type> assertionTimeout <as_value>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <sensor type> is one of the following numeric sensor types:\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b Sensor types Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 absoluteHumidity Absolute humidity sensors\
relativeHumidity Relative humidity sensors\
temperature Temperature sensors\
airPressure Air pressure sensors\
airFlow Air flow sensors\
vibration Vibration sensors\
<value> is the value for the specified threshold of the specified sensor type. Note that diverse sensor\
types use different measurement units.\

\f0\b \cf5 Sensor types Measurement units\

\f1\b0 \cf3 absoluteHumidity g/m^3 (that is, g/m
\fs9\fsmilli4980 3
\fs20\fsmilli10020 )\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 395
\fs20\fsmilli10020 Sensor types Measurement units\

\f1\b0 \cf3 relativeHumidity %\
temperature Degrees Celsius ( ) or Fahrenheit ( ),\
depending on your measurement unit settings.\
airPressure Pascal (Pa) or psi, depending on your\
measurement unit settings.\
airFlow m/s\
vibration g\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <hy_value> is the deassertion hysteresis value applied to the specified sensor type.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <as_value> is the assertion timeout value applied to the specified sensor type. It ranges from 0 to 100\
(samples).\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - Default Upper Thresholds for Temperature\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 It is assumed that your preferred measurement unit for temperature is set to degrees Celsius. Then the\
following command sets the default Upper Warning threshold to 20 and Upper Critical threshold to 24\
for all temperature sensors.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 defaultThresholds temperature upperWarning 20\
upperCritical 24\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Sensor Threshold Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A sensor configuration command begins with 
\f3\i sensor
\f1\i0 . You can use the commands to configure the threshold,\
hysteresis and assertion timeout values for any sensor associated with the following items:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Inlets\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Inlet poles (for three-phase PDUs only)\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Overcurrent protectors\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Environmental sensors\
It is permitted to assign a new value to the threshold at any time regardless of whether the threshold has\
been enabled.\
