\f2\fs18 \cf5 Examples\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section illustrates several environmental sensor threshold configuration examples.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 1 - Upper Critical Threshold for a Temperature Sensor\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets the Upper Critical threshold of the environmental "temperature" sensor with the\
ID number 2 to 40 degrees Celsius. It also enables the upper critical threshold if this threshold has not been\
enabled yet.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 sensor externalsensor 2 temperature upperCritical 40\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 402 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0 Example 2 - Warning Thresholds for Inlet Sensors\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets both the Upper Warning and Lower Warning thresholds for the inlet 1 RMS\
current.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 sensor inlet 1 current upperWarning 20 lowerWarning 12\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Warning threshold for the inlet 1 RMS current is set to 20A. It also enables the upper warning\
threshold if this threshold has not been enabled yet.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Lower Warning threshold for the inlet 1 RMS current is set to 12A. It also enables the lower warning\
threshold if this threshold has not been enabled yet.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 3 - Upper Thresholds for Overcurrent Protector Sensors\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets both the Upper Critical and Upper Warning thresholds for the 2nd overcurrent\
protector.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 sensor ocp 2 current upperWarning enable upperCritical 16\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Critical threshold for the 2nd overcurrent protector's RMS current is set to 16A. It also\
enables the upper critical threshold if this threshold has not been enabled yet.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Warning threshold for the 2nd overcurrent protector's RMS current is enabled.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An actuator configuration command begins with 
\f3\i actuator
\f1\i0 . You can configure the name and location\
parameters of an individual actuator.\
You can configure various parameters for one actuator at a time. See

\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page\
408).\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572

\f0\b\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf5 Type Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 Free form <coordinate> is a string comprising up to 24\
ASCII printable characters, and it must be\
enclosed in quotes.\
Rack units <coordinate> is an integer number in rack units.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is the ID number assigned to the actuator. The ID number can be found using the Legrand PDU web\
interface or CLI. It is an integer starting at 1.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <name> is a string comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters. The <name> variable must be\
enclosed in quotes when it contains spaces.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <coordinate> is a string comprising up to 24 ASCII printable characters, and it must be enclosed in\
quotes.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 There are two types of values for the <z_label> variable, depending on the Z coordinate format you set:\

\f3\i Note: To specify the Z coordinate using the rack units, see 
\f0\i0\b \cf5 Setting the Z Coordinate Format for\
Environmental Sensors
\f3\i\b0 \cf3  (on page 323).\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <description> is a sentence or paragraph comprising up to 64 ASCII printable characters, and it must be\
enclosed in quotes.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - Actuator Naming\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command assigns the name "Door lock" to the actuator whose ID number is 9.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 actuator 9 name "Door lock"\

\fs24 Server Reachability Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can use the CLI to add or delete an IT device, such as a server, from the server reachability list, or\
modify the settings for a monitored IT device. A server reachability configuration command begins with\

\f3\i serverReachability
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Adding a Monitored Device\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command adds a new IT device to the server reachability list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability add <IP_host> <enable> <succ_ping>\
<fail_ping> <succ_wait> <fail_wait> <resume> <disable_count>\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the ping monitoring feature for the newly\
added device.\
false Disables the ping monitoring feature for the newly\
added device.\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <IP_host> is the IP address or host name of the IT device that you want to add.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <enable> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <succ_ping> is the number of successful pings for declaring the monitored device "Reachable." Valid\
range is 0 to 200.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <fail_ping> is the number of consecutive unsuccessful pings for declaring the monitored device\
"Unreachable." Valid range is 1 to 100.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <succ_wait> is the wait time to send the next ping after a successful ping. Valid range is 5 to 600\
(seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <fail_wait> is the wait time to send the next ping after a unsuccessful ping. Valid range is 3 to 600\
(seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <resume> is the wait time before the Legrand PDU resumes pinging after declaring the monitored device\
"Unreachable." Valid range is 5 to 120 (seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <disable_count> is the number of consecutive "Unreachable" declarations before the Legrand PDU\
disables the ping monitoring feature for the monitored device and returns to the "Waiting for reliable\
connection" state. Valid range is 1 to 100 or 
\f3\i unlimited
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Deleting a Monitored Device\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command removes a monitored IT device from the server reachability list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability delete <n>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is a number representing the sequence of the IT device in the monitored server list.\
You can find each IT device's sequence number using the CLI command of 
\f8 show\
serverReachability
\f1  as illustrated below.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 405\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019January 2019\

<succ_number>\

<fail_number>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability modify <n> waitTimeAfterSuccessfulPing\
<succ_wait>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify the wait time after a unsuccessful ping:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability modify <n> waitTimeAfterUnsuccessfulPing\
<fail_wait>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify the wait time before resuming pinging after declaring "Unreachable":\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability modify <n> waitTimeBeforeResumingPinging\
<resume>\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Modify the number of consecutive "Unreachable" declarations before disabling the ping\
monitoring feature:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability modify <n> numberOfFailuresToDisable\
<disable_count>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <n> is a number representing the sequence of the IT device in the server monitoring list.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <IP_host> is the IP address or host name of the IT device whose settings you want to modify.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i true 
\f1\i0 or 
\f3\i false
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 true Enables the ping monitoring feature for the\
monitored device.\
false Disables the ping monitoring feature for the\
monitored device.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 406 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f2\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <succ_number> is the number of successful pings for declaring the monitored device "Reachable." Valid\
range is 0 to 200.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <fail_number> is the number of consecutive unsuccessful pings for declaring the monitored device\
"Unreachable." Valid range is 1 to 100.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <succ_wait> is the wait time to send the next ping after a successful ping. Valid range is 5 to 600\
(seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <fail_wait> is the wait time to send the next ping after a unsuccessful ping. Valid range is 3 to 600\
(seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <resume> is the wait time before the Legrand PDU resumes pinging after declaring the monitored device\
"Unreachable." Valid range is 5 to 120 (seconds).\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <disable_count> is the number of consecutive "Unreachable" declarations before the Legrand PDU\
disables the ping monitoring feature for the monitored device and returns to the "Waiting for reliable\
connection" state. Valid range is 1 to 100 or 
\f3\i unlimited
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - Server Settings Changed\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command modifies several ping monitoring settings for the second server in the server\
reachability list.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serverReachability modify 2 numberOfSuccessfulPingsToEnable 10\
numberOfUnsuccessfulPingsForFailure 8\
waitTimeAfterSuccessfulPing 30\

\f3\i Variables:\

acceptable.\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623

\fs24 Serial Port Configuration Commands\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Setting the Baud Rates\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following commands set the baud rate (bps) of the serial port labeled CONSOLE on the Legrand PDU\
device. Change the baud rate before connecting it to the desired device, such as a computer, a Raritan's\
P2CIM-SER, through the serial port, or there are communications errors. If you change the baud rate\
dynamically after the connection has been made, you must reset the Legrand PDU or power cycle the\
connected device for proper communications.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Determine the CONSOLE baud rate:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serial consoleBaudRate <baud_rate>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <baud_rate> is one of the baud rate options: 
\f3\i 1200
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 2400
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 4800
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 9600
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 19200
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 38400
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 57600
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i 115200
\f1\i0 .\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command sets the CONSOLE baud rate of the Legrand PDU device's serial port to 9600 bps.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 serial consoleBaudRate 9600\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Multi-Command Syntax\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 To shorten the configuration time, you can combine various configuration commands in one command to\
perform all of them at a time. All combined commands must belong to the same configuration type, such as\
commands prefixed with 
\f3\i network
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i user modify
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i sensor externalsensor
\f1\i0  and so on.\
A multi-command syntax looks like this:\

\f8 <configuration type> <setting 1> <value 1> <setting 2> <value 2> <setting 3> <value\
3> ...\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Example 1 - Combination of IP, Subnet Mask and Gateway Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following multi-command syntax configures IPv4 address, subnet mask and gateway for the network\
connectivity simultaneously.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network ipv4 ipAddress 192.168.84.225 subnetMask 255.255.255.0\
gateway 192.168.84.0\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The IP address is set to 192.168.84.225.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The subnet mask is set to 255.255.255.0.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The gateway is set to 192.168.84.0.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 2 - Combination of Upper Critical and Upper Warning Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following multi-command syntax simultaneously configures Upper Critical and Upper Warning thresholds\
for the RMS current of the 2nd overcurrent protector.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 409
\f8\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 config:#
\f1  
\f8 sensor ocp 2 current upperCritical disable upperWarning 15\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Critical threshold of the 2nd overcurrent protector's RMS current is disabled.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Warning threshold of the 2nd overcurrent protector's RMS current is set to 15A and enabled\
at the same time.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 3 - Combination of SSID and PSK Parameters\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This multi-command syntax configures both SSID and PSK parameters simultaneously for the wireless\
feature.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 network wireless SSID myssid PSK encryp_key\

\f3\i Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The SSID value is set to myssid.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The PSK value is set to encryp_key.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example 4 - Combination of Upper Critical, Upper Warning and Lower Warning Settings\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following multi-command syntax configures Upper Critical, Upper Warning and Lower Warning\
thresholds for the outlet 5 RMS current simultaneously.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 sensor outlet 5 current upperCritical disable upperWarning enable\
lowerWarning 1.0\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f3\i\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Results:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Critical threshold of outlet 5 RMS current is disabled.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Upper Warning threshold of outlet 5 RMS current is enabled.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 The Lower Warning threshold of outlet 5 RMS current is set to 1.0A and enabled at the same time.\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Load Shedding Configuration Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
A load shedding configuration command begins with 
\f3\i loadshedding
\f1\i0 .\
Unlike other CLI configuration commands, the load shedding configuration command is performed in the\

\f3\i administrator mode
\f1\i0  rather than the configuration mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page\
296).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 410 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Enabling or Disabling Load Shedding\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command determines whether to enter or exit from the load shedding mode.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 loadshedding <option>\

\f1 After performing the above command, Legrand PDU prompts you to confirm the operation. Press 
\f8 y
\f1  to\
confirm or 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation.\
To skip the confirmation step, you can add the "/y" parameter to the end of the command so that the\
operation is executed immediately.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 loadshedding <option> /y\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i enable
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i disable
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 start Enter the load shedding mode.\
stop Quit the load shedding mode.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command has the Legrand PDU enter the load shedding mode.\

\f8 config:#
\f1  
\f8 loadshedding start\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Power Control Operations\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
Outlets on the Legrand PDU can be turned on or off or power cycled through the CLI.\
Besides, you can cancel the power-on process while the Legrand PDU is powering on ALL outlets.\
You must perform this operation in the 
\f3\i administrator mode
\f1\i0 . See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on\
page 296).\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 411
\fs24 Turning On the Outlet(s)\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command turns on one or multiple outlets.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 power outlets <numbers> on\

\f1 To quicken the operation, you can add the parameter "/y" to the end of the command, which confirms the\
operation.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 power outlets <numbers> on
\f1  
\f8 /y\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <numbers> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , an outlet number, a list or a range of outlets.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Switches ON all outlets.\
A specific outlet\
number\
Switches ON the specified outlet.\
A comma-\
separated list of\
outlets\
Switches ON multiple, inconsecutive or\
consecutive outlets.\
For example, to specify 7 outlets -- 2, 4, 9, 11, 12,\
13 and 15, type 
\f8 outlets 2,4,9,11-13,15
\f1 .\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A range of\
outlets with a\
hyphen in\
between\
Switches ON multiple, consecutive outlets.\
For example, to specify 6 consecutive outlets -- 3,\
4, 5, 6, 7, 8, type 
\f8 outlets 3-8
\f1 .\
If you entered the command without "/y", a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Then:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 y
\f1  to confirm the operation, OR\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 412 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs24 Turning Off the Outlet(s)\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This section applies to outlet-switching capable models only.\
This command turns off one or multiple outlets.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 power outlets <numbers> off\

\f1 To quicken the operation, you can add the parameter "/y" to the end of the command, which confirms the\
operation.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 power outlets <numbers> off
\f1  
\f8 /y\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <numbers> is one of the options: 
\f3\i all
\f1\i0 , an outlet number, a list or a range of outlets.\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 all Switches OFF all outlets.\
A specific outlet\
number\
Switches OFF the specified outlet.\
A comma-\
separated list of\
outlets\
Switches OFF multiple, inconsecutive or\
consecutive outlets.\
For example, to specify 7 outlets -- 2, 4, 9, 11, 12,\
13 and 15, type 
\f8 outlets 2,4,9,11-13,15
\f1 .\
A range of\
outlets with a\
hyphen in\
between\
Switches OFF multiple, consecutive outlets.\
For example, to specify 6 consecutive outlets -- 3,\
4, 5, 6, 7, 8, type 
\f8 outlets 3-8
\f1 .\
If you entered the command without "/y", a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Then:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 y
\f1  to confirm the operation, OR\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Actuator Control Operations\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 An actuator, which is connected to a dry contact signal channel of a DX sensor, can control a mechanism or\
system. You can switch on or off that mechanism or system through the actuator control command in the\
CLI.\
Perform these commands in the administrator or user mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on\
page 296).\

\f8 #

\f1  
\f8 /y\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623

The ID number is available in the Legrand PDU web interface or using the show command in the CLI. It\
is an integer between 1 and 32.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If you entered the command without "/y", a message appears, prompting you to confirm the operation. Then:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 y
\f1  to confirm the operation, OR\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Type 
\f8 n
\f1  to abort the operation\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Unblocking a User\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If any user is blocked from accessing the Legrand PDU, you can unblock them at the local console.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To unblock a user:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Log in to the CLI interface using any terminal program via a local connection. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 With HyperTerminal\

\f1\i0\b0 \cf3 (on page 295).\
2. When the Username prompt appears, type 
\f8 unblock
\f1  and press Enter.\
3. When the "Username to unblock" prompt appears, type the name of the blocked user and press Enter.\
4. A message appears, indicating that the specified user was unblocked successfully.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Resetting the Legrand PDU\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can reset the Legrand PDU to factory defaults or simply restart it using the CLI commands.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Restarting the PDU\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command restarts the Legrand PDU. It is not a factory default reset.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To restart the Legrand PDU:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. 2. Ensure you have entered administrator mode and the # prompt is displayed.\
Type either of the following commands to restart the Legrand PDU.\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 reset unit\

\f1 3. -- OR --\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 reset unit
\f1  
\f8 /y\

\f1 4. If you entered the command without "
\f8 /y
\f1 " in Step 2, a message appears prompting you to confirm the\
operation. Type y to confirm the reset.\
Wait until the Username prompt appears, indicating the reset is complete.\

\f3\i Note: If you are performing this command over a USB connection, re-connect the USB cable after the reset\
is completed, or the CLI communications are lost.\

\f0\i0\b\fs18 \cf5 416 Legrand PDU User Guide

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following commands restore all settings of the Legrand PDU to factory defaults.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To reset Legrand PDU settings after login, use either command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 #
\f1  
\f8 reset factorydefaults\

\f1 -- OR --\

\f8 #
\f1  
\f8 reset factorydefaults
\f1  
\f8 /y\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Network Troubleshooting\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The Legrand PDU provides 4 diagnostic commands for troubleshooting network problems: 
\f3\i nslookup
\f1\i0 , 
\f3\i netstat
\f1\i0 ,\

\f3\i ping
\f1\i0 , and 
\f3\i traceroute
\f1\i0 . The diagnostic commands function as corresponding Linux commands and can get\
corresponding Linux outputs.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Entering Diagnostic Mode\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Diagnostic commands function in the diagnostic mode only.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To enter the diagnostic mode:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Enter either of the following modes:\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  Administrator mode: The # prompt is displayed.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  User mode: The > prompt is displayed.\
2. Type 
\f8 diag
\f1  and press Enter. The diag# or diag> prompt appears, indicating that you have entered the\
diagnostic mode.\
3. Now you can type any diagnostic commands for troubleshooting.\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Quitting Diagnostic Mode\

\f4\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To quit the diagnostic mode, use this command:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 diag>
\f1  
\f8 exit\

\f1 The # or > prompt appears after pressing Enter, indicating that you have entered the administrator or user\
mode. See 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Different CLI Modes and Prompts
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on page 296).\

\f0\b\fs24 \cf5 Diagnostic Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The diagnostic command syntax varies from command to command.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 417\

\f6\b0 \cf2 January 2019
\f2 \cf5 Querying DNS Servers\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax queries Internet domain name server (DNS) information of a network host.\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 nslookup <host>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the name or IP address of the host whose DNS information you want to query.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Showing Network Connections\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax displays network connections and/or status of ports.\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 netstat <option>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <option> is one of the options: 
\f3\i ports
\f1\i0  or 
\f3\i connections
\f1\i0 .\

\f0\b \cf5 Option Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 ports Shows TCP/UDP ports.\
connections Shows network connections.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f2 \cf5 Testing the Network Connectivity\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This ping command sends the ICMP ECHO_REQUEST message to a network host for checking its network\
connectivity. If the output shows the host is responding properly, the network connectivity is good. If not,\
either the host is shut down or it is not being properly connected to the network.\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 ping <host>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the host name or IP address whose networking connectivity you want to check.\

\f3\i Options:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 You can include any or all of additional options listed below in the ping command.\

\f0\b \cf5 Options Description\

\f1\b0 \cf3 count <number1> Determines the number of messages to be\
sent. <number1> is an integer number\
between 1 and 100.\
size <number2> Determines the packet size. <number2> is\
an integer number in bytes between 1 and\
65468.\
timeout <number3> Determines the waiting period before\
timeout. <number3> is an integer number in\
seconds ranging from 1 to 600.\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 418 Legrand PDU User Guide
\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The command looks like the following when it includes all options:\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 ping <host> count <number1> size <number2> timeout <number3>\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Tracing the Route\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 This command syntax traces the network route between your Legrand PDU and a network host.\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 traceroute <host>\

\f3\i Variables:\

\f2\i0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  \cf3 <host> is the name or IP address of the host you want to trace.\

\f2\fs18 \cf5 Example - Ping Command\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 The following command checks the network connectivity of the host 192.168.84.222 by sending the ICMP\
ECHO_REQUEST message to the host for 5 times.\

\f8 diag>
\f1  
\f8 ping 192.168.84.222 count 5\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Retrieving Previous Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 If you would like to retrieve any command that was previously typed in the same connection session, press\
the Up arrow ( ) on the keyboard several times until the desired command is displayed.\

\f6\fs18 \cf2 January 2019\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Automatically Completing a Command\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 A CLI command always consists of several words. You can easily enter a command by typing first word(s) or\
letter(s) and then pressing Tab or Ctrl+i instead of typing the whole command word by word.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To have a command completed automatically:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Type initial letters or words of the desired command. Make sure the letters or words you typed are\
unique so that the CLI can identify the command you want.\
2. 3. Press Tab or Ctrl+i until the complete command appears.\
If there are more than one possible commands, a list of these commands is displayed. Then type the full\
command.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b Examples:\

\f2\b0 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Example 1 (only one possible command):\

\f1\b0 a. Type the first word and the first letter of the second word of the "
\f8 reset 
\f1 command -- that is, 
\f8 reset f
\f1 .\
b. Then press Tab or Ctrl+i to complete the second word.\

\f2 \cf5 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Example 2 (only one possible command):\

\f1\b0 a. Type the first word and initial letters of the second word of the "
\f8 security\
enforceHttpsForWebAccess
\f1 " command -- that is, 
\f8 security enf
\f1 .\
b. Then press Tab or Ctrl+i to complete the second word.\

\f8 factorydefaults
\f1 "\

\f0\b\fs18 \cf5 Legrand PDU User Guide 419
\f2\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \uc0\u61623 
\f1  
\f0\b \cf3 Example 3 (more than one possible commands):\

\f1\b0 a. Type only the first two words of the "
\f8 network ipv4 gateway xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
\f1 " command -- that\
is, 
\f8 network ipv4.\

\f1 b. Then press Tab or Ctrl+i one or two times, a list of possible commands displays as shown below.\

\f8 gateway
\f1  
\f8 interface
\f1  
\f8 staticRoutes\

\f1 c. Type the full command "
\f8 network ipv4 gateway xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
\f1 ", according to the onscreen\
command list.\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Logging out of CLI\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 After completing your tasks using the CLI, always log out of the CLI to prevent others from accessing the\
CLI.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To log out of the CLI:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. 2. Ensure you have entered administrator mode and the # prompt is displayed.\
Type 
\f8 exit
\f1  and press Enter.\

\f0\b \cf5 420 Legrand PDU User Guide
\fs63\fsmilli31980 \cf2 Using SCP Commands\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 You can perform a Secure Copy (SCP) command to update the Legrand PDU firmware, do bulk\
configuration, or back up and restore the configuration.\

\f2\fs24 In This Chapter\

\f1\fs20\fsmilli10020 Firmware Update via SCP .................................................................... 420\
Bulk Configuration via SCP .................................................................. 420\
Backup and Restore via SCP ............................................................... 421\
Downloading Diagnostic Data via SCP ................................................ 422\
Uploading or Downloading Raw Configuration Data............................ 424\

\f0\b\fs32\fsmilli16020 \cf4 Firmware Update via SCP\

\f1\b0\fs20\fsmilli10020 \cf3 Same as any Legrand PDU firmware update, all user management operations are suspended and all login\
attempts fail during the SCP firmware update. For details, see 
\f7\i\b \cf5 Updating the Legrand PDU Firmware
\f1\i0\b0 \cf3  (on\
page 260).\
Warning: Do NOT perform the firmware upgrade over a wireless network connection.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b To update the firmware via SCP:\

\f1\b0 \cf3 1. Type the following SCP command and press Enter.\

\f8 scp <firmware file> <user name>@<device ip>:/fwupdate\

\f1 2. 3. 4. 
\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f3\i <firmware file>
\f1\i0  is the Legrand PDU firmware's filename. If the firmware file is not in the current\
directory, you must include the path in the filename.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  
\f3\i <user name>
\f1\i0  is the "admin" or any user profile with the Firmware Update permission.\

\f5 \uc0\u61607 
\f1  <device ip> is the IP address or hostname of the Legrand PDU where you want to upload the\
specified file.\
Type the password when prompted, and press Enter.\
The system transmits the specified firmware file to the Legrand PDU, and shows the transmission speed\
and percentage.\
When the transmission is complete, it shows the following message, indicating that the Legrand PDU\
starts to update its firmware now. Wait until the upgrade completes.\

\f8 Starting firmware update. The connection will be closed now.\

\f4 \cf4 \uc0\u61572 
\f1  
\f0\b SCP example:\

\f8\b0 \cf3 scp pdu-px2-030410-44599.bin admin@192.168.87.50:/fwupdat}
